Objectives:  
• To develop multidimensional dissemination & communication (D&C) plan, to deliver D&C activities;  
• To undertake stakeholder base building and engagement activities via the BIC consortium and BBI-JU; 
• To develop and deliver scalable training and capacity-building activities to underpin skills development;  
• To identify early adopters and post-project opportunities; 
• To contribute to existing and emerging standards. 
 
Task 7.1 – Multidimensional D&C and stakeholder engagement activities (DEC, ALL PARTNERS). This task, 
led by DEC and to which all partners participate, will deliver effective D&C and stakeholder engagement activities 
as per outline in section 2.2. DEC will work across the technical WPs to identify, develop and publish agreed 
dissemination materials to the identified target audiences (TAs) in a timely manner.  
ST7.1.1 Dissemination plan and activities [DEC]: DEC will develop, implement, monitor and update the Plan for 
Exploitation and Dissemination of Results (PEDR) a document setting the strategic directions of the dissemination 
activities in order to reach the project ’s goals and involve the TAs. Dissemination actions will be developed to 
maximise the promotion of non-confidential results and knowledge generated during the project to as many relevant 
actors as possible. As indicated in Table 2-5 on page 40, we foresee the preparation and publication of scientific 
publications / papers, participation in R&D and business conferences, etc.  
ST7.1.2 Communication plan and activities [DEC]: A series of strategic and targeted communication activities, 
described in Section 2.2, will promote BioSPRINT and its results to multiple TAs, using all appropriate channels, 
to reach stakeholders, raise awareness, and encourage engagement with BioSPRINT. This will require a range of 
‘push’ and ‘pull’ communications approaches, and facilitation of two-way exchange of views and information with 
stakeholders, including: the creation, maintena nce and update of (i) the project identity/brand [ by EBOS], (ii) the 
project’s public website and portal [by EBOS]; (ii) Set-up and management of 4 social media groups and channels 
(Facebook, LinkedIn, Twitter, YouTube) and production of content including promotional videos (1/year by DEC); 
(iii) implementation of all communication campaigns, including production and distribution of quarterly newsletters, 
regular social media posts, factsheets, success stories, brochures, press releases, etc.  
ST7.1.3 Value chain stakeholder base building, BIC/BBI-JU engagement and liaison with other BBI and 
bioeconomy projects [DEC]: DEC. with support from other BIC members (i.e. AEP, FhG, NIC, UOULU, UPM) 
will promote the interests of BBI -JU to address the needs for a strong and efficient bioeconomy, in particular the 
goals of the BIC SIRA 2017. DEC will also ensure timely dissemination of the results and findings from the project 
via the B BI-JU’s newsletter, workshop sessions, and events. In addition, liaison activities will be undertaken  to 
identify common interests with other BBI and bioeconomy -related projects, in view of organising joint events and 
clustering results and efforts.  
Task 7.2 - Training, Education & Capacity Building programme (TECBP) (NIC, DEC, AEP, EBOS, UOULU, 
UNEW). This task, led by NIC and with participation of academic, research and industrial partners UOULU, UNEW, 
DEC and AEP, will deliver the BioSPRINT TECBP as outlined in Section 2.2. Materials will be developed in line 
with best practises in this area , and will also consider results from the SusChem Educate to Innovate initiative. 
Activities include delivery of 4 online modules, 4 training & capacity-building workshops as well as the BioSPRINT 
Summer School. NIC will also ensure the materials are suitable for inclusion in relevant academic courses. When 
delivering the TECBP, attention will be paid to select a broad gender-balanced audience among academia, industry 
and other BBI JU stakeholders. EBOS will support the task with computer-aided tools and ICT development. DEC 
will support the task in organizing the events (online and onsite). 
ST7.2.1 TECBP plan & strategy [DEC]: DEC will develop, implement, monitor and update the TECBP plan and 
strategy, setting the strategic directions of the programme in order to reach the project goals and involve the TAs. 
ST7.2.2 BioSPRINT online TECBP [NIC]: In this subtask, implemented during the 2nd year of the project, NIC, 
together with the WP1-4 leaders and EBOS, will develop, implement and deliver 4 online-access training modules 
in English  language, introduced via live webinars, to a large academic, research and industrial audience.  The 
modules will focus on one or several of the BioSPRINT focus areas for PI of biorefining operations. 
ST7.2.3 TECBP workshops [NIC]: In this subtask, implemented during the 3rd year of the project, NIC, togethe r 
with the WP1-4 leaders, will organise 4 TECBP workshops, in 4 countries: FI, IT, SI and UK. A large academic, 
research and industrial audience, gender-balanced, will be targeted with min. 20 external participants in attendance

Task 7.3 – Identification of early adopters, post-project opportunities and business plan (MAT, DEC, IRIS, 
UPM). Under the leadership of MAT, assisted by DEC, IRIS and UPM, this task aims at expanding the initial 
business model into a feasibility study and elaborate business plan – which will be partly validated via the project’s 
partners. It aims at understanding past, present and future industry trends, approaches and tactical/strategic responses 
and at producing a detailed SWOT analysis, paving the way for the realisation of a feasibility and business plan. As 
for continuity of funding routes and commercial sustainability, partners will aim a t sustaining the effort in 
BioSPRINT beyond M48 with the required third -party actors across Europe, as well as reaching out to potential 
investors, venture capitalists and European acceleration catalysts. Partners will work at identifying opportunities for 
financing the post-project work necessary to progress the technologies and processes to TRL 7, and later TRL 9. 
Task 7.4 - Contribution to existing and emerging standards (DEC, AEP, UNEW, UPM). Building on the 
Roadmap for PI standardisation developed as part of the completed IbD project, T7.4 seeks to make an impactful 
contribution to relevant industry standards. Several consortium partners are members of standardisation bodies and 
can influence the standardisation process by preparing factual data, proposals, and draft protocols for adoption by 
technical committees (TCs). This will be supported by Mr. Mavroyiannos, Standards officer, EAB member.                                                             
ST7.4.1 PI Standards – CWA [DEC+UNEW]: Under the leadership of DEC, the consortium will establish a CWA 
on ‘PI for Biorefining Processes ’. TM UNEW will also contribute so as to ensure contribution to standardisation 
follows a bottom-up approach from the technical WPs, particularly in relation with PI equipment and processes.  
ST7.4.2 Product Standardisation [AEP, UPM]: Contributions to standard s related to products, i.e. resins, polyols 
and polymers will also be made by AEP and UPM. 
Role of the main partners: DEC leads WP7 primarily supported by NIC and EBOS, and with contribution from 
all partners. Justification of resources: Over 48 months, DEC will assign 1 person (50% time) while NIC and EBOS

Objective:  
• To coordinate all project activities by (a) Ensuring the project meets its contractual commitments (deliverables, 
quality, etc.); (b) Providing sound Technical Management; (c) Performing sound Quality Assurance (QA) & Risk 
Management (RM); (d) Planning and performing Innovation and Data management. 
 
Task 8.1 - Project coordination and reporting (DEC, AEP, IFEU, NIC, UOULU, UNEW, UPM) 
Overall day-to-day contractual, financial and administrative management of the project incl. resources allocation.  
ST8.1.1 Overall Project coordination and financial reporting [DEC]: The Project Coordinator (PC) will be assisted 
by the WP leaders and Proj ect Steering Team (PST) members to manage the operation of all WPs ensuring their 
compliance to the time plan. Activities include: (a) Preparation of bi -annual management reports as described in 
Section 3.2, ( b) Budget controlling and accounting, ( c) Organisation of meetings and minutes keeping, and ( d) 
Monitoring of the progress according to the contractual schedule.  
ST8.1.2 Liaison with EC and BBI-JU, preparation and submission of deliverables, review reports and questionnaires 
[DEC]: This subtask is dedicated to liaison with the EC, the submission of high-quality deliverables, the organisation 
of the review meetings as well as the preparation and submission of continuous reporting and periodic progress 
reports. Furthermore, this task will coordinate the preparation of the answer to the annual BBI JU questionnaires. 
ST8.1.3 EAB management [DEC]: W.r.t the EAB, under the coordination of DEC, it will help steer the commercial 
and scientific direction of the project. It is composed of 6 external experts as indicated in Section 3.2. Physical 
meetings will be organised in M1, M12, M24, M36 and M48 with virtual teleconference meeting in M6, M18, M30 
and M42. Minutes will be produced including a review of the technological, policy, legal or security challenges and 
needs uncovered during the EAB meetings. 
Task 8.2 - Technical Management (UNEW, NIC). Due to the technical complexity of the project as well as the 
breadth of the validation efforts to be undertaken, technical management will be undertaken b y UNEW (PI 
expertise). UNEW will: (a) Monitor the technical progress of the project according to contractual schedule, (b) Liaise 
with the EAB on technical matters, (c) Monitor the preparation of technical deliverables, (d) Prepare technical 
project reviews and deliver Technical Reports. (e) Provide expertise in the technical WPs, while also assisting in the 
technical soundness and feasibility assessment of all the project’s tasks. Any slowdown or technical/technological 
problem will be rapidly addressed and risk mitigation strategies issued. 
 
Task 8.3 - Quality Assurance (QA) & Risk Management (RM) (EBOS, DEC). This task, led by EBOS, executes 
the QA & RM processes for the project. W.r.t QA, EBOS will establish and implement QA procedures with 
particular focus on monitoring review activities built into the WPs and submitting quality reports annually. The 
quality plan specifies the quality procedures, internal and external peer reviews, control, monitoring and reporting 
activities. W.r.t RM, EBOS will establish and implement a plan and procedures for RM and reporting, covering both 
the project operational risks and  the framework barriers/risks, and monitor the progress to ensure that proactive 
measures are taken to mitigate risks. Attention was taken during the proposal’s elaboration to ensure that no more 
than 3 deliverables will be delivered per month. 
Task 8.4 – Innovation, IPR & Data Management (MAT, EBOS). W.r.t. Innovation Management, MAT, 
supported by EBOS, will identify and manage innovation from the project, advising the PC and partners on the scope 
and potential of the innovations arising and paying attention to discerning IPR at regular checkpoints. Work includes 
the monitoring of the progress of development of innovative tools/services throughout the project.  
ST8.4.1 Innovation and IPR management  [MAT]: To ensure sustainability, exploitation and marketability of the 
project’s results, MAT designs the IPR protection strategy, considering aspects defined in Section 2.2 and establishes 
IPR management procedures and associated activities. All IP produced is monitored and the potential IPR attached 
to them (e.g. copyright, patent, etc.) are verified and cleared for the project's good execution. MAT also ensures that 
confidentiality agreements and all the partners’ defined IPRs (foreground and background) in the Consortium 
Agreement (CA) are fully respected. MAT also advises on  IPR protection activities, in view of strategically 
protecting the most compelling innovation from BioSPRINT.  
ST8.4.2 Data management plan and monitoring [ EBOS]: W.r.t. Data Management, EBOS will be responsible for 
preparing and monitoring the implementation of the Data Management Plan (DMP), determining how innovation 
and research data are handled during and after the project, the application of the data privacy and pseudo -
anonymisation techniques, privacy preserving data mining, security and consent management which will be applied 
to data collected in the project. The DMP will contain information related to the types of data the project will generate 
/ collect (including personal data if applicable), the data standards to be used and how partners might exploit the 
data, thus setting robust management procedures and supporting GDPR compliance. 
ST8.4.3 Ethics, Gender and cross-cutting priority monitoring [EBOS]: This subtask led by EBOS, ensures that (a) 
project’s activities are ethically sound and that data from participants is stored according to EU and  national 
regulations to ensure data privacy; (b) Monitors Gender & the cross -cutting priorities of the project . W.r.t Ethics, 
under the coordination of EBOS, the task identifies and addresses ethical concerns responsibly and produces an 
information sheet and informed consent form (drafts provided in Annex 3).   
Role of the main partners: DEC leads WP8, overseeing the management and execution of the project , primarily 
supported by the PMB. Justification of resources: Over 48 months, both DEC and EBOS will assign ~1 person 
part-time (50%).

3.2 Management structure, milestones and procedures  
3.2.1 Organisational Structure and Decision Making  
The successful implementation of a collaborative project such as BioSPRINT, with 12 partners from 8 countries, 
requires efficient, well -documented and structured project management procedures. The BioSPRINT project 
management structure, as shown in Figure 3. 2, is designed to meet the objectives of all stakeholders, including the 
EC, by creating responsiveness to the evolving needs of the project.  
In particularly, it will: (a) Ensure that the project meets its contractual obligations. This will entail continuous 
progress monitoring, managed by the Project Coordinator (PC), communication and a shared understanding of roles 
& responsibilities. (b) Facilitate the delivery of high-quality research and innovation. Central to achieving this will 
be the coordination of the activities of the technical partners and the integration of their results ; and (c) Maximise, 
measure and validate the impact of the system on the target audiences, both within and beyond the technology 
enhanced learning research and industry communities. 
The management structure, whose management functions, roles and procedures are part of the CA, consists of:  
• Council of Partners (CoP). Chaired by the PC, the CoP includes representatives from each and every partner, 
having the authority to make decisions on behalf of their respective organisations in terms of overall strategy and

resources allocated to the project. The CoP appoints the EAB. The CoP meets every six months. The meeting agenda 
includes: (a) Report by the PC, (b) Report by the QRM Manager on quality and risks issues, (c) Reports by the WP 
Leaders on technical implementation issues, (d) Approval of annual and final reports, (e) Approval of year ly 
implementation plans, and (f) Decisions on specific items. 
Project Steering Team (PST). The PST consists of the managers of the project, as listed in Table 3-2c below, who 
bring a wealth of experience in coordinating EU projects. The PST ensures that the project will achieve its objectives 
and satisfy the needs of the EC, the consortium and the Bioeconomy as a whole. The PST focuses on consortium 
management issues, including Technical Management, QA, the Consortium Agreement (CA), roles and 
responsibilities, audit certificates, ethics, gender issues, societal questions and liaison with 3rd parties and the EC.  
• Work Package Leaders (WPL) . WPLs lead a given WP from WP1 to WP 7 and report to the PC, who is the 
leader of WP8. Tasks include: to produce detailed work plans and progress reports, to guard the timely and effective 
execution of the WP work and ensure that deliverables meet the quality standards. WPLs also review WP results and 
flag up any underperformance. They provide input to management reports and represent the WP at the PST. Names 
of the WPL are listed in Table 3-2c below. 
• External Advisory Board (EAB). The EAB will offer impartial scientific advice, support the PST and advise the 
consortium on social, environmental, technologi cal, legal and economic factors that may influence the innovation 
management of BioSPRINT. It will be chaired by one of its members, elected upon the EAB’s first meeting in M1. 
The following persons have confirmed their interest in and willingness to participate in the BioSPRINT EAB through 
Letters of Support provided in Annex 2 (from page 130): 1. Dr. Tom Granström, Head of St1 Research, ST1 OY, 
Finland; 2. Dr. Markus Rarbach , Head of Business Line Biofuels & Derivatives , Clariant, Germany. 3. Dr. Ed 
Marshall, General Manager Biorefinery R&D, Sappi Biotech Limited, United Kingdom;  4. Mr. Marios 
Mavrogiannos, Standards Officer, Cyprus Organisation for Standardisation, Cyprus. ; 5. Mr. Darren Gobby , 
Principal Process Engineer, Johnson Matthey, UK; 6. The 6th seat of the EAB is reserved for a member of the Board 
of the BIC consortium.  
This management structure was deemed appropriate for BioSPRINT for the following reasons: (a) It ensures strategic 
management and decision making (PST) as well as appropriate interfacing with the EC (PC); (b) It provides effective 
management of the day -to-day running of the project (WPL) and its resources ; (c) It manages the overall 
technological development and its potential risks in an integrated manner (Technical Manager & WPLs, Quality & 
Risk Manager); (d) It clearly attributes and distributes responsibilities for implementing work, reporting progress, 
controlling the deliverables and the milestones (Table 3 -2a, page 66), and managing and mitigating risks (Table 3 -
2b, page 67); (e) It addresses the interdisciplinary aspects of the project (technological, innovation, legal, ethical, 
etc.); (f) It provides decentralised management (appointment of qualified managers) to ensure we deliver high impact.

Progress reporting 
Internal (within Consortium): Every beneficiary commits to write bi-annually a management report, which will 
describe the technical and management project work done, listing effective time  spent on the project , mention 
difficulties, milestones and deliverables (or contributions to deliverables in case of joint deliverables) that have been 
reached, publications, travel and visits. The PC will be able to track both overall budget burn rates, as well as identify 
potential problems with individual organisations as a result of this report.  
External (to BBI JU): The PC will coordinate, consolidate and submit to the EC the periodic (e.g. M18, M30) and 
final reports (due 2 months after end of grant term), deliverables and the financial reports as needed.  
Project communications and meetings : The consortium recognises that a vital factor towards the successful 
management of BioSPRINT, is effective communication. A kick-off meeting (KOM) is planned in M1. PST face-to-
face project meetings will be convened every 6 months. CoP meetings and PST meetings will coincide in time, in 
which case the day before the CoP meeting, PST members will gather to present  an overview and table any critical 
decisions to be taken at the CoP. Additional cross -team, meetings at WP level, and face to face meetings will be 
organised when necessary, and teleconferences will be arranged at much frequent time intervals, as needed. Thus, in 
total 9 face-to-face PST/CoP meetings (i.e. in M1, M6, M12, M18, M24, M30, M36, M42 and M48) are anticipated. 
Daily communications will primarily use email and VoIP/Skype/GoToMeeting tools. A project mailing list will be 
established; WPLs may also set up their own distribution lists. Contact details for all personnel involved will be 
available from the tools established by the PC, where information, ideas and documents will be shared.  
Consortium agreement (CA): It will be concluded between all members of the consortium, as dictated by EU rules, 
prior to the signature of the Grant Agreement (GA). The CA will be based on the common DESCA model and will 
supplement the Description of Action, covering topics that are important for the delivery of the project and the 
management of knowledge between partners, but are not specific to the consortium’s contract with the EC 
Decision-making mechanisms & conflict resolution: In the course of the project, the consortium will have to agree 
on and develop technic al, scientific and commercial ideas and specifications. Most decisions about the work to be 
carried out have been made at proposal and so will be subject to the GA signed with the EC. Decision making will 
strive for consensus: agreement will usually be reached, followed by official confirmation via electronic mail, letter 
or written minutes. For important issues, the agreement may take the form of a short report , signed by those 
responsible for decision-making. Conflict prevention techniques will be used to  avoid problems. Where consensus 
cannot be reached, conflict resolution procedures will be actioned. The specific roles described above will resolve 
and/or implement the necessary actions, according to the following process: (1) Issues will first be addressed within 
the relevant WP through discussion chaired by the WPL. (2) If this fails, the issue will be presented by the WPL 
either to the PC, TM or the CoP depending on the nature of the problem (i.e. administrative, technical or 
business/strategic). (3) The relevant board will resolve the issue through a majority vote, with the board chair holding 
a casting vote. The EAB will be involved in case of high-level scientific disputes. (4) Conflicts that cannot be resolved 
through those principles will be mediated by an external expert in view of reaching consensus. (5) As a last resort, 
disputes will be handled according to the dispute resolution provision set forth in the CA. 
 
3.2.3 Innovation Management  
The Innovation, IPR & Transferability Manager (IM), Mr. Mladen Crnomarkovic will be responsible for Innovation 
management as part of T 8.4. Specific measures to engender an innovation culture within the project will be: (a) 
Project meetings will include sessions on emerging technologies/approaches to generate novel ideas for research and 
to ensure applied knowledge transfer to industrial partners, and inform future research decisions, and (b) To foster a 
commercial exploitation culture among partners to maxim ise the identification, assessment and execution of 
opportunities to deliver impact from research outputs. In addition, the EAB will be responsible for continuous review 
of the research progress , being provided with reports at 6 -month intervals from the CoP,  in order to identify new 
opportunities for innovation, grow the engagement with industrial partners, and seek new collaborations. 
 
3.2.4 Critical Implementation Risks and Mitigation actions (Table 3-2b) 
The project implementation plan, produced at the start of the project, is subject to revision in the course of the project, 
in accordance with the procedures for project re-planning outlined in this section. One of the main reasons that project 
re-planning may be necessary is as a result of regular risk assessment in the project. The initial list of risks presented 
in Table 3 -2b is a start to this process; more detailed assessment of risks will  be carried out regularly, based on 
practical experiences in running the project. Risk management will be  the responsibility of the QRM (Gotelenne 
Piaton, EBOS) in collaboration with the PC, TM and IM, and WPLs . The management of risks will be part of the

regular PST meetings. Table 3-2b describes a representative set  of the risks, their probability (P) and impact (I) 
(L=Low, M=Medium and H=High) and proposed risk mitigation measures 
Table 3-2b: Critical risks for implementation 
Description of risk Proposed risk-mitigation measures P Ι WP 
Frequent / important fouling of 
membranes and surfaces 
A thorough analysis of all three HMC streams will reveal the typical 
foulants. Efficient prefiltration step in lab tests will be conducted to remove 
them. CFD model will help prevent concentration polarisation and fouling 
by optimizing the process hydrodynamics and using photocatalytic 
degradation and/or precipitation of the foulants. 
L M 1 
The upstream purification is not 
as effective or efficient as desired. 
Screening experiments and availability of different membranes and 
materials (ceramic, zeolites) ensure that the best purification methods can 
be selected. The purification can also be improved by hy bridisation with 
other separation method(s). In addition, DoE tools will be used to select the 
process parameters (T, p, pH, etc.) optimizing the purification efficiency. 
M M 1 
Green antisolvents and salting 
agents used in SDR encourage 
sugars to precipitate alongside 
lignin thus reducing effectiveness 
of separation. 
A number of antisolvents and salting out reagents will be carefully screened 
for their ability to preferentially isolate lignin from the C5/C6 sugars. 
Appropriate data (e.g. solubility, metastable zone) of relevant species will 
be gathered experimentally or from literature and used in a decision matrix 
to select the most effective ones.  
M H 1 
Poor Data quality in the  
machine learning catalyst design 
Prior to experimental work, the possible error sources will be identified and 
their impact to collected data will be minimised. The ML methods are 
selected and adapted based on data quality and may incorporate pre -
processing techniques or simpler model str uctures in order to utilise the 
information content as efficiently as possible. 
L M 2 
Extraction-reaction coupling in 
sugar dehydration step may 
increase process complexity due 
to hybridisation step. 
A good understanding of the influence of operation parameters will be 
developed during the modelling of this hybridisation step to allow 
technology development and performance optimisation.  
M L 2 
Sugar conversions to 
furans take excessively 
long times. 
Different reactor technologies will be evaluated for their suitability, with 
those providing the best residence times being selected for 
implementation in the pilot scale development unit. 
L L 3 
Preceding reactor activities are 
lagging behind schedule, which in 
turn delays the development of 
downstream. 
Downstream separation development is initially performed on model 
reaction mixtures, which may be anticipated, based on input reactor 
compositions, as well as some ideali sed operation (equilibri um, non -
intensified, etc.), thus reducing time to development. 
M M 3 
Purity of furfural and 5 -HMF is 
not high enough for the efficient 
synthesis of resins and polyols. 
Feedbacks from WP4 will facilitate iterative steps for the choice of the best 
combination of streams, catalytic conversion processes and downstream 
purification providing the required purity. 
M M 2,3,
4 
First round resins and polyols are 
not REACH compliant. 
A REACH assessment will be carried out to check the compliancy with the 
REACH definition of ‘polymer’. In case of non-compliancy, the synthesis 
protocols are modified to meet the ‘polymer’ definition. 
L H 4 
The bio-based polyols and foams 
do not meet the required industrial 
specifications and performances 
related to end applications. 
Bio-based polyols will be optimi sed and validated against commercial 
benchmarks. Proper formulation is foreseen to improve the foams’ 
properties while maximizing their bio -based content, also through the 
synergistic addition of bio-polyols from other sustainable sources 
L M 4 
The kinetics of the polymerisation 
step for the novolac resin may be 
too slow for significant monomer 
conversions to be reached in a 
single pass in the SDR. 
Temperature can be increased to enable faster kinetics. A recirculation loop 
can also be implemented to enable multiple passes in the reactor. In the 
worst-case scenario, a pre -polymerising step can be implemented so that 
the SDR can be more beneficially a pplied in the finishing and often more 
challenging stages of the process.

project partners and external experts will be used instead. M L 6

reaching out to an insufficient number of participants. Recruitment will 
start early so as to intensify if targets are not met.

3.3 Consortium as a whole  
 The BioSPRINT consortium has been mobilised around the requirements of the call to intensify biorefining 
operations for lignocellulosic feedstock. 
Geography. The consortium comprises 12 partners from 8 European countries from all 4 main European regions: 
Northern Europ e (9%), Western Europe (50%), Eastern Europe (9%), and Southern Europe (32%). It involves 
research, innovation and industrial organisations, with discernible domain expertise in the technology areas, which 
are being researched and leveraged into BioSPRINT. 
 
Complementary expertise. The BioSPRINT consortium (Figure 3.4) unites the necessary multidisciplinary 
knowledge, expertise, skills, and resources to constitute a representative value chain of actors, which together are 
capable of achieving the project’s ambitious objectives. These organisations have a strong applied approach to their 
research and 6 of them are members of BIC and committed to working closely with the European Bioeconomy for 
realising an efficient and sustainable transition to a greener economy . There is no conflictive overlap among the 
consortium and each participating organisation has a clearly defined role in the project. The consortium is made of: 
• Academic and research technology organisations (DEC, UOULU, FhG, UNEW, NIC) capable of providing 
the PI, biochemistry, PSE, and dissemination  expertise necessary to exercise an applied research push within the 
project. The aim is to leverage existing assets from previous research and further advance these assets in collaboration 
with industries and SMEs. DEC is an experienced H2020 PC with an established reputation of excellence, which has 
guided dozens of successful collaborative projects across Europe.  
• Industrial actors (UPM, PFR, AEP), representing the feedstock provision and intermediary end -user sides of 
the value chain, taking charge of providing HMC feedstock streams (UPM), leading the validation and integration 
into value chains of the BioSPRINT biorefining concept (UPM) and the development of innovative bio renewable 
novolac and resole-type resins (PFR) and bio-based polyols (AEP), well-suited to replace fossil-based counterparts 
in the near future.  
• Biotechnology, process simulation, engineering, control and ICT SMEs ( ADSC, IRIS, EBOS ) with 
complementarity expertise, high technological capacity  and market orientation. These partners can contribute the 
technology push (especially in the context of scale-up, integration and validation of the results), but also absorb the 
knowledge generated, in order to quickly industrialise the project’s outputs.  
• Two modelling, TEA and LCA SME actors (MAT, IFEU ) with strong modelling , LCA  and consulting 
experience, in order to undertake the TEA, ILCSA, Innovation & IPR management and pave the way towards 
commercial exploitation. 
Strong presence of SMEs. There is a strong presence of SMEs (46% of consortium members) leading a number of 
tasks especially in the technical development, absorbing 39% of the total budget, (Figure 3.4).  
Gender balance aspects. BioSPRINT is also fully committed to promoting and fostering gender balance in research 
teams and project decision -making bodies. The BioSPRINT project team  includes 37% of women . In addition, 
BioSPRINT will aim at achieving gender balance for its TECBP and will take all necessary measures to encourage 
and secure equal participation of women. A number of the key management and decision -making positions within 
the project organisational structure have been assigned to highly qualified women ( Dr. Boodhoo as Technical 
Manager, Ms. Fuchs as D&C Manager, Dr. Nina Rimmel as WP5 leader, Ms. Piaton as QRM).   
 
 
 
deliverables; Management issues

long experience in coordination and management of large consortia.  
Conflicts and disputes between the partners will be resolved immediat ely

The consortium was carefully assembled to represent complementary skills

In short, BioSPRINT unites sufficient reputable actors from the academic & scientific fields, as well as from

3.4 Resources to be committed 
In relation to the project budget, it has been built using a bottom-up methodology, whereby it is based on actual costs 
for staff, equipment depreciation and other goods and services. There is a logical budget distribution among the 
partners and each has mobilised the necessary staff/person months (Table 3.4a) to get the job done in a competitive 
timeframe. Subcontracting is only foreseen in relation to the establishment of the CWA and UOULU analysis costs. 
In relation to personnel costs, differences in costs between the different EU regions, reflect differences in the cost of 
living. There is sufficient budget for mobility of developers and industrialists between sites which is important for 
knowledge exchange, as well as for practi cal on-site validation. There is an appropriate budget allocated to D&C, 
knowledge management and project coordination activities. Considering that there are 12 partners, and a competitive 
48-month work plan, a requested EC Contribution of € 4,998,015 and a total budget of € 5,740,640, with in-kind 
contributions estimated at €353,200 and additional investments estimated at >€300M; a good value for high impact. 
Furthermore, the budget of industrial partners PFR and UPM equal €742,625 (with 0% funding rate) or 13% of total 
budget.

4.1.1 DECHEMA GESELLSCHAFT FUER CHEMISCHE TECHNIK UND BIOTECHNOLOGIE E.V. 
Short Name DEC 
 
Country Germany 
Type Research Organisation 
Website www.dechema.de 
Short Profile 
DECHEMA Gesellschaft für Chemische Technik und Biotechnologie e.V. (Society for Chemical Engineering and 
Biotechnology), (DEC) brings together experts from a wide range of disciplines, institutions and generations to 
stimulate scientific exchange in chemical engineering, process engineering and biotechnology. DEC identifies 
and evaluates emerging technological trends and facilitates the transfer of research results into industrial 
applications. DEC aims to boost the competitiveness of Germany and Europe as a pre-eminent business location 
for chemistry and biotechnology, to position chemical engineering, process engineering and biotechnology in the 
public and political spheres as important key technologies and problem solvers, and also to increase awareness of 
the benefits of these disciplines for society.  
 
DEC is also the hub of an interdisciplinary network of topic -oriented committees, organizing events and 
professional development courses for all who are interested in a specialized subject area. DEC’s network has over 
5.800 members – individuals, institutions and companies - and is the place where future trends in research and 
technology are identified, debated in-depth and promptly translated into recommendations for action. 
 
DEC is the expert network for chemical engineering and biotechnology in Germany. This non-profit professional 
society represents these fields in science, industry, politics and society. Around 100 subject divisions and working 
parties offer a forum for knowledge exchange among experts, based on trust.  
  
 
1 ACA = Academic, Higher or secondary education establishment, IND= Industrial partner, NGO = Non -Governmental Organisation, 
PO=Public Organisation, RTO = Research & Technology Organisation, SME = Small to Medium sized Enterprise 
2 Affiliated to BIC via membership in the ‘Chamber of Commerce and Industry of Stajerska’, Slovenia

DEC will involve its Biotechnology Section and ProcessNet, the joint platform for chemical engineering, which 
are the forums where scientists, engineers, students, companies and institutions meet for knowledge exchange and 
discussion. Biotechnology and the bioeconomy have been focus areas of DECHEMA since the early 1970s. The 
DECHEMA Biotechnology Section has more than 1,800 members  and promotes scientific exchange in 
biotechnology, chemical engineering, and process engineering. DEC seeks out and evaluates new technological 
trends and provides support for translating research results into industrial applications. 
 
DEC’s involvement will be steere d by the group " Research and Project Coordination " which analyses and 
evaluates innovative developments in all fields of technology, facilitates the partner -brokerage for project 
definition and subsequently offers coordination projects and management of pr ojects. This group is working at 
both the national and European level.  The Group will leverage DEC’s 25+ years of experience in identifying and 
closing technological gaps, in facilitating communication between research, industry and the public sector and in 
supporting the market uptake of innovation, organizing a broad range of events, from specialists’ workshops to 
large international conferences with 3000 and more participants, setting-up online resources such as the knowledge 
base on nanomaterials  funded and supported by the German Federal Ministry of Education and Research (BMBF), 
and, broadly, facilitating and disseminating research and innovation in the chemical and biotechnology sectors on 
a daily basis. DEC also has experience with innovation management and grant application for numerous 
bioeconomy-related projects and has been working together with partners such as FNR (Agency for Renewable 
Resources) and DBU (Deutsche Bundesstiftung Umwelt). 
 
DEC has extensive experience with coordinating European projects - DEC is/has been the Coordinator of eight 
projects, in the areas of chemistry, bio economy, process industry and energy efficiency, including, among others:  
- KETBIO: ‘A novel cluster model to bring KE Y ENABLING BIOTECHNOLOGY research closer to 
markets and society’, 5 Partners, (01/10/2017 - 31/03/2020); 
- RoadToBio: ‘Roadmap for the Chemical Industry in Europe towards a Bioeconomy’, 4 Partners, 
(01/05/2017 - 30/04/2019); 
- WaterWatt: ‘Improvement of energy efficiency in industrial water circuits using gamification for online 
self-assessment, benchmarking and economic decision support’, 6 Partners, (01/04/2016 – 31/03/2019); 
- CarbonNext: ‘The Next Generation of Carbon for the Process Industry’, 3 Partners, (0 1/09/2016 - 
31/08/2018); 
- E4WATER: ‘Economically and Ecologically Efficient Water Management in the European Chemical 
Industry’, 20 Partners, (01/05/2012 - 30/04/2016). 
 
DEC is/was also a participant in the following relevant H2020 projects: 
- ENERGY-X: ‘Transformative chemistry for a sustainable energy future’, 13 Partners, (01/03/2019 – 
29/02/2020); 
- VOLATILE: ‘Biowaste derived volatile fatty acid platform for biopolymers, bioactive compounds and 
chemical building blocks’, 21 Partners, (01/12/2016 - 30/11/2020); 
- INSPIREWater: ‘Innovative Solutions in the Process Industry for next generation Resource Efficient 
Water management’, 11 Partners, 01/10/2016 - 31/03/2020); 
- AceForm4.0: ‘Activating Value Chains for EU leadership in FORMulation Manufactur ing 4.0’, 7 
Partners, (01/10/2016 - 30/09/2018); 
- BioLinX: ‘Creating links to speed -up innovation in the bio economy’, 9 Partners, (01/07/2015 - 
30/06/2018); 
 
DEC is an Associate Member of the Bio-based Industries Consortium (BIC) which represents the private sector in 
the Bio-based Industries Joint Undertaking (BBI JU), the Public -Private Partnership (PPP) with the European 
Commission. DEC also represents Germany at the European Federation of Chemical Engineering, which promotes 
scientific collaboration supporting the work of engineers and scientists in 30 European countries. In addition, DEC 
is a member of the European Federation of Biotechnology  (EFB) which p romotes the safe, sustainable and 
beneficial use of the life sciences, as well as research and innovation at the cutting edge of biotechnology. EFB 
provides a forum for interdisciplinary and international cooperation, in order to facilitate an informed dia logue 
between scientists, the biotechnology industries and the public. 
 
DEC is a founding member of SusChem, the European Technology Platform (ETP) for Sustainable Chemistry. 
SusChem’s mission is to initiate and inspire European chemical and biochemical innovation to respond effectively 
to societal’s challenges by providing sustainable solutions. SusChem has close ties with two PPPs: the ‘Sustainable 
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 75 
 
Process Industry through Resource and Energy Efficiency’ ( SPIRE) PPP and the Biobased Industries Joint 
Initiative (BBI JU) . 
Role in the project 
DEC will lead WP8 'Project Coordination' acting as the project coordinator, assuming responsibility for the 
Coordination and Management of the project, including the planning, monitoring, assessment, reporting, 
evaluation and continuous assessment of all Work Packages (WPs), their associated task s, and the overall 
execution of the implementation plan. DEC will also coordinate the External Advisory Board (EAB) steering the 
commercial and scientific direction of the project.  
 
From the technical point of view, DEC will participate in  WP1 ‘ Intensification of Upstream Purificatio n’ 
contributing in the analysis of treated hemicellulose streams. In particular, DEC will undertake the liaison with the 
involved industrial providers of feedstocks: UPM, FhG, Clariant.  
 
Under WP2 ‘Intensification of Catalytic Conversion’ DEC will be involved to ensure optimal knowledge transfer 
towards the dissemination & exploitation WP (WP7) and integrate the findings of WP2 into the Training, 
Education & Capacity-Building Programme (TECBP). Similarly, DEC will be involved in WP3 ‘Intensification 
of Downstream Purification’ and WP4 ‘Development of Biorenewable Resins and Polymerisation 
Intensification’.   
 
Within WP5 ‘Validation, Process Simulation & Integration ’ DEC will lead the task dedicated to  the 
transferability case study with Clariant Sunliquid® stream . DEC will monitor the development of a case study 
report on processing the Clariant streams with the recommendations on the integration of the most efficient process 
operation variants. DEC will collect the data from previous technical WP (1 –4) activities, in order to prepare a 
summary characteristic comparison  of all the  key characteristics for consequent upstream/reaction/downstream 
processing (hemicellulose, decomposed oligo -/monomer sugars, furans, biomass -derived organic acids, lignin, 
inorganics (ashes), density, viscosity, mixture surface tension, etc.).  
 
In WP6 ‘Integrated Lifecycle Sustainability Assessment’ DEC will be in charge of the system analysis and 
description aiming to provide the goal and scope of the integrated sustainability assessment as well as all initial 
definitions, settings and system description, including technological parameters. DEC will also participate in the 
Integrated life cycle sustainability assessment  so as to ensure that all the results from previous analyses  are 
integrated to identify and depict the most sustainable pathways among the BioSPRINT value chains compared to 
all reference systems. 
 
As a hub of an interdisciplinary network of topic -oriented committees, organizing events and professional 
development courses for specialized subject area s, DEC will also lead WP7 ‘ Dissemination and Exploitation’ 
aiming to develop the project’s multidimensional dissemination & communication (D&C) plan and deliver D&C 
activities; undertake stakeholder base building and stakeholder engagement activities via BBI-JU and also  
contribute to existing and emerging standards. As part of WP7, DEC will work with all partners across to identify, 
develop and publish agreed dissemination materials to the identified target audiences in a timely manner.  In 
particular, DEC will develop, implement, monitor and update the Plan for Exploitati on and Dissemination of 
Results (PEDR) a document setting the strategic directions of the dissemination activities in order to reach the 
project goals by supervising a series of strategic and targeted communication activities, promot ing BioSPRINT 
and its results to multiple audiences, using all appropriate channels, to reach stakeholders, raise their awareness, 
and encourage engagement with the project. In addition, DEC will promote the interests of BBI-JU to address the 
needs for a strong and efficient bio economy. With regards to standardisation, DEC will be in cha rge of the 
activities seeking to make an impactful contribution to industry Standards related to P rocess Intensification (PI) 
equipment and processes, building on the RoadMap for PI standardisation developed as part of the IbD project, as 
well as product standards related to resins, polyols and polymers . DEC will be mainly responsible for the 
establishment of a CENELEC Workshop Agreement (CWA) on ‘PI for Biorefining processes’.

4.1.2 AEP POLYMERS SRL 
Short Name AEP 
 
Country Italy 
Type Small or medium-size enterprise 
Website www.aeppolymers.com 
Short Profile 
AEP Polymers SRL (AEP) is an innovation -based company, focused on applied R&D in the field of biobased 
building blocks, polymers and formulations for industrial applications. AEP Polymers was founded in 2013 and 
has 4 highly trained employees with long -standing expertise in fib re-reinforced composites, epoxy resins, 
polyurethanes (rigid and flexible PU foams, compact PU), elastomers, adhesives and a wide variety of 
functionalized building blocks. 
 
Sustainability is AEP’s way of working to generate added value to companies though  the creation of new 
substances and materials starting from renewable resources, from plant -derived fatty acid oils to bio -aromatics, 
like Cashew Nut Shell Liquid (CNSL) and lignin. Naturally -occurring peculiar chemical structures are a perfect 
starting point to pursue innovative chemical routes and formulation approaches, delivering performing materials 
for demanding industrial applications. The starting materials are selected or extracted from by-products of the food 
and forestry industry and chemically m odified to obtain the desired properties. The functionalized materials are 
then formulated in high bio -content resin systems ready for benchmarking against commercial petro -based 
products. 
 
The novelty of the approach is coupling material selection and syn thetic approach in a way that ensures that the 
materials will be industrially scalable and performing on par with commercially available products. The product 
development approach often combines phenols, carbohydrates and fatty acids in order to obtain materials that are 
technically and economically viable. 
 
AEP’s business model exploits the newly generated IP on biobased polymers through licensing, with a number of 
bio-based products and formulations already being produced and commercialized by industrial partners. AEP has 
extensive synthetic expertise, having developed biobased polyols, amines and other functionalized materials from 
a wide variety of biobased oils both within funded R&D projects and industrial cooperations. 
 
AEP will focus on the conversio n of the monomers previously obtained from hemicellulose (furfural, 5 -HMF,) 
into novolac and resole -type resins for application in wood boards, as well as into Mannich -base, novolac-type, 
polyester and polyether-polyester polyols for rigid polyurethane foams. 
The optimization of the synthetic protocols and their successive upscaling will be carried out based on the 
feedbacks from application-oriented formulation and testing work. AEP will investigate the performance benefits 
provided by the newly developed bio-based polyols, also benchmarking them against commercially available 
petro-based polyols for targeted industrial applications.  
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 78 
 
AEP is a Full Member of the Bio -based Industries Consortium (BIC) which represents the private sector in the 
Bio-based Indus tries Joint Undertaking (BBI JU), the Public -Private Partnership (PPP) with the European 
Commission. 
Role in the project 
AEP’s role will be focused on the formulation of new and innovative biorenewable resins from5-HMF and furfural, 
as well standards applicable to products and the identification of exploitation pathways. 
 
In WP3 ‘Intensification of Downstream Purification’, AEP will participate in the preparatory processing actions 
for downstream so as to ensure efficient liaison with the polymerisation activities at WP4. 
 
Leveraging expertise in the synthesis of biobased polyols, developed in industrial partnerships and strengthened 
within BBI JU projects (e.g. ReInvent, where AEP has been develo ping bio-polyols from fatty acids-based oils) 
AEP will lead WP4 ‘Development of Biorenewable Resins and Polymerisation Intensification’  monitoring the 
activities to convert a) the monomers obtained in WP3 (furfural, 5 -HMF) into novel novolac and resole -type 
polymers (500 g scale) for application in wood boards and b) 5-HMF into novel Mannich-base, polyester polyols 
and polyether-polyester polyols respectively (500 g scale) for rigid polyurethane foams and Polyesters for coatings. 
In addition, AEP will lead the development of testing of bio -based polyols . In particular, AEP will use the 
monomers previously obtained from hemicellulose (furfural, 5-HMF) to develop and study: a) novolac and resole-
type resins for application in wood boards and b) Mannich-base, novolac-type, polyester and polyether-polyester 
polyols for rigid polyurethane foams. Under WP4, AEP will also take care of the formulation and testing of rigid 
polyurethane foams based on the new bio-polyols. 
 
As part of WP5 ‘Validation, Process Simulation & Integration’ , AEP will support the integration of the 
developed concepts and technologies for the UPM stream and the Organosolv stream. In addition, AEP will lead 
and monitor the scale-up of optimal product formulations, selecting the most promising polyols, pre-polymers and 
resins and their developed syntheses replicated through the multiple repeatable batches in small –medium bench 
scale. This will support the modelling, simulation and scale -up of polymerization reactor units, for pilot plant 
engineering and optimization enduing.  
 
In WP6 ‘Integrated Lifecycle Sustainability Assessment’, AEP will contribute in the process and product safety 
assessment, assessing specifically the safety of new bio-based products, taking into account also their production 
processes. The use of less hazardous reagents and/or solvents (e.g. less volatile, more environmentally friendly, 
having lighter labelling) will be considered and, for each optimized production process, a safety protocol will be 
prepared, providing the operators with a list of instructions and personal protective equipment (PPE). 
 
As part of WP7 ‘Dissemination and Exploitation’ , AEP will contribute in the Training, Education & Capacity 
Building programme (TECBP)  development and implementatio n by organizing one of the 4 BioSPRINT 
workshops for knowledge transfer, capacity -building, training and education. Also, AEP will be involved in the 
effort to make an impactful contribution to industry standards related product standards. In addition, as part of 
WP7, AEP will support the Coordinator in the Multidimensional dissemination, communication and stakeholder 
engagement activities in order to develop the project’s multidimensional dissemination & communication (D&C) 
plan and undertake stakeholder base building and stakeholder engagement activities via BBI-JU. 
 
In WP8 ‘Project Coordination’, AEP will support the Project Coordinator DEC, in the o verall coordination, 
management and reporting as the leader of WP4.

Relevant Infrastructure 
The company’s laboratory is located in the AREA Science Park of Trieste (Italy), one of the most important multi-
sectorial technological parks in Europe, that offers services aimed at strengthening the integrated regional research 
infrastructure, creating new networks and increasing researchers’ mobility and companies’ internationalization. 
AEP’s laboratory covers 210 sq. meters and has the equipment to cover the following activities: 
• Chemical reactors (design and synthesis of new molecules, scale-up and optimization up to 5L volume) 
• HPLC-GPC (chemical characterization) 
• Automatic titrator + Karl Fisher (characterization and QC analyses) 
• Ovens (controlled curing of thermosetting polymers) 
• Viscometer (viscosity, polymer/formulation stability) 
• DSC (glass transition temperature, enthalpy of reaction, fusion)  
• Universal Testing Machine (tensile, flexural, compression, adhesion tests) 
• Small scale fire reaction tests (UL-94 and similar) 
• Polymer formulation and reactivity evaluation (string time, pot life, gel time, tack free time, etc.) 
• Production of small-scale prototypes (foams, composites, coatings) 
• Chemical resistance tests, thermal ageing tests 
 
Other tests are available via continuous collaboration with local research institutions: 
• High temperature mechanical characterization 
• Rheological characterization of non-Newtonian fluids 
• UV weathering 
• Optical microscopy, TEM, SEM 
• NMR analysis 
 
In BioSPRINT as an in-kind contribution, AEP will install a new chemical laboratory and purchase equipment 
(new chemical reactor, ancillary and testing instruments) with capacity to convert biobased fractions into chemical 
building blocks, polymers and reactive formulations, for a total value of €140,000. The new lab will serve as an 
addition to the company’s lab infrastructure.

4.1.3 DYNAMIC & SECURITY COMPUTATIONS SL 
Short Name ADSC  
Country Spain 
Type Small or medium-size enterprise 
Website www.analisis-dsc.com 
Short Profile 
DYNAMIC & SECURITY COMPUTATIONS 
SL (ADSC) is a mechanical engineering and 
service consultancy company specializing in 
process engineering and applications related to 
fluid mechanics, heat transfer, bulk materials 
using Computer Aided Engineering (CAE) 
tools such as Computational Fluid Dynamics 
(CFD), FEA, and Discrete Elements 
Modelization (DEM).  
 
The company was founded in 2002 in Madrid, 
Spain. ADSC has expertise in the analysis of 
complex industrial processes involving fluids in 
tasks of  Basic Engineeri ng, Failure 
Engineering; Analysis, Optimization and Scale-
up of Industrial Processes. 
 
ADSC is the exclusive distributor for CAE 
(Computer Aided Engineering) software in 
Spain and Portugal. The computer aided engineering or CAE, is a group of informatic programs, which is able to 
analyze and simulate the engineering designs incorporating them in a computer, in order to evaluate their 
characteristics, properties, feasibility and profitability. The goal is to optimize the design, the production costs and 
also reduce the number of the necessary tests so as to obtain the desired product. 
 
As an engineering and consultancy company ADSC is involved in the development of a wide range of projects: 
- Industrial processes optimization, from the structural, thermal or fluid dynamic point of view; 
- Industrial products design optimization from the structural, thermal or fluid dynamic point of view; 
- Structural static or dynamic analysis, fatigue, etc.; 
- Tunnel and stations ventilation and risk analysis study using S. E. S. and CFD tools; 
- Contingency analysis (contaminants/radioactive particles dispersion analysis); 
- A technological partner in R&D projects. 
 
For the development and implementation of its projects ADSC uses several tools such as CAD (Computer Aided 
Design), Computational meshers, CFD (Computational Fluid Dynamics) or fluid mechanics, Structural or thermal 
mechanics (Mecánica) using finite elements method, SES (Subway Environment Simulator) and Discrete 
Particles.  
 
In the project, ADSC’s strong knowledge and experience of CFD will be leveraged in order to perform tasks of 
basic engineering, analysis, optimization and scale-up of process engineering.  
 
CFD is a software tool, used to simulate the behavior of the fluid-flows, heat transfer, chemical reaction and other 
related physical phenomena. The CFD has the ability to solve the equations of the fluid flow in the region or 
domain of interest, with specified conditions in the boundaries of the domain.  CFD is widely used by engineers 
and scient ists for a wide range of applications in the following domains: Process industry (mixers, chemical 
reactors, heat exchangers, pumps, valves, scrubbers, fermenters), Energy (combustion, nuclear plant 
thermohydraulic analysis), Renewable energy (solar therma l, eolic energy, tidal energy), Hydraulics 
(turbomachinery and pipes, erosion, working limit analysis) and Chemistry (agitators, fermenters, bubble columns, 
reactors, carbonators).  
 
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 82 
 
ADSC usually works for customers in the Iberian Peninsula or as subcontractor to other international customers 
in need of specialized engineering services when facing operational or design problems. ADSC is a horizontal 
engineering company with references in most of the main economic sectors such as energy, civil engineering, 
hydraulics, chemistry, etc.

Role in the project 
ADSC will mostly perform tasks of process systems engineering (PSE), and analysis, optimization and scale -up 
of process engineering using advanced modelling tools such as CAE (CFD, FEA, DEM, etc). Different CAE 
scenarios will be performed so that other partners in the consortium will evaluate the CFD vs Experiment 
comparison.  
 
In WP1 ‘Intensification of Upstream Purification’, ADSC will participate in the identification of upstream scale-
up challenges via process systems engineering (PSE) tools , providing CFD tools and simulations. Under WP2 
‘Intensification of Catalytic Conversion’, ADSC will lead the i dentification of reaction scale -up challenges via 
process systems engineering tools for the catalytic conversion phase of BioSPRINT. In particular, the reaction and 
extraction processes to be intensified in WP2 will be analysed using CFD tools at lab-scale in order to provide a 
set of recommendations on how to scale-up an intensified reaction and extraction reactor. These recommendations 
will include the thermo-fluid behaviour of the reactor using CFD tools, the control anal ysis and PAT techniques 
on the later-on pilot plant equipment. 
 
Similarly, in WP3 ‘Intensification of Downstream Purification’ , and WP4 ‘Development of Biorenewable 
Resins and Polymerisation Intensification’ , ADSC will participate in the task relating to the i dentification of 
downstream scale-up challenges, and polymerisation scale-up challenges respectively. 
 
In WP5 ‘Validation, Process Simulation & Integration’, ADSC will contribute in the integration of the developed 
concepts and technologies for the Organosolv stream (FhG) with an emphasis on the validation of reaction and 
downstream purification technologies. 
 
As part of WP7 ‘Dissemination and Exploitation’, ADSC will support the Coordinator in the Multidimensional 
dissemination, communicat ion and stakeholder engagement activities  in order to develop the project’s 
multidimensional dissemination & communication (D&C) plan and undertake stakeholder base building and 
stakeholder engagement activities via BBI-JU. 
 
ADSC will lead T2.4 ‘Identification of reaction scale-up challenges via process systems engineering tools’, and 
participate in the following tasks: 
− T1.4 Identification of upstream scale-up challenges via process systems engineering (PSE) tools 
− T3.4 Identification of downstream scale-up challenges

Short Name EBOS

Short Profile 
EBOS Technologies Ltd (EBOS) is an innovative and client-focused Information Technology (IT) SME software 
house with head offices in Cyprus and branch offices in Ireland and in the UK. EBOS is dedicated in providing 
comprehensive and cost-effective technologically-advanced e-business software solutions to enterprise customers 
worldwide. 
 
EBOS product portfolio provides a wide range of Windows and web -based customisable business solutions 
targeted for the enterprise market. EBOS core product offering, WiseBOS Enterprise Resource Planning (ERP), 
is a state -of-the-art comprehensive software Suite, that offers complete, innovative, and proven solutions for 
enterprises of all sizes who want to thrive in the new digital era. WiseBOS ERP Suite is designed to adapt in 
flexible ways to the ever -changing business nee ds of companies, unleashing the real potential of having fully 
integrated solutions that are fully-aligned with their business directives.  
 
EBOS is heavily investing in beyond the state -of-the-art technologies, thereby accelerating future digital 
innovation. EBOS Research & Development (R&D) division is focused on future -oriented research in a broad 
area of activities and domains, such as ICT, wireless communication networks including 5G, Next Generation 
Internet Technologies, Big Data analytics, A rtificial Intelligence, Machine Learning, Cybersecurity, Augmented 
& Virtual Reality as well as Energy efficiency. EBOS long-term expertise and experience of 16+ years have been 
boosted though the company’s successful engagement in cutting -edge research projects funded primarily by the 
European Commission. In collaboration with large international research teams, EBOS has managed to become a 
highly respected and reliable partner and has made significant achievements at the frontier of ICT development, 
to drive industry development and business model success via technological breakthroughs.  
EBOS is a member of 5G -PPP and a member of the NESSI (Networked European Software and Services 
Initiative), NEM (New European Media), NetWorld 2020 European Technology P latforms and NGI (Next 
Generation Internet) initiative. In such platforms, EBOS is an active member of the SME Working Groups, where 
it provides input to the EU Institutions on research actions and technology matters of particular importance to the 
software and interactive technologies domain, specifically in relation to their relevance for SMEs. 
EBOS is also a member of Vision 2020 - Crowdhelix, a pan-European Open Innovation platform connecting an 
international network of universities, research organisations & companies, with 377 member organisations to date.. 
In January 2019, the Ministry of the Finance of Cyprus has distinguished eBOS Technologies with the ‘Innovative 
SME’ certificate in recognition of its efforts in research, development and innovation activities. The certification 
is the result of an independent evaluation that confirmed eBOS engages an important share of the company’s 
financial and human assets in continuous research and innovation efforts. Nation-wide, eBOS Technologies is the 
13th SME recipient of the award, highlighting the rigor and ambition of the criteria to be achieved. 
 
In BioSPRINT, EBOS will involve two of departments, the Research and Development department  (R&D) 
coordinating the involvement of EBOS in research projects imple mented in collaboration with international 
partners, and the Creativity department providing a range of professional services including Website design. The 
R&D department will provide expertise mainly in the areas of Interactive dashboards, Data Visualisation & Data 
analytics, Quality Assurance and Risk Assessment, as well as Open -standards APIs development, application 
integration and interoperability.

Role in the project 
EBOS will provide ICT development related to the application of Machine Learning to optimal catalyst 
development and the use of advanced data analytics and visualisation techniques for effective and efficient 
monitoring of complex systems.  
 
In WP2 ‘Intensification of Catalytic Conversion’, EBOS will participate in the catalyst development using HTP 
Methods in order to deliver robust catalyst formulations for integrated conversion of C5 and C6 sugars into a single 
reactor, coupled with extraction of reactive furan intermediated. In particular, EBOS will leverage assets from 
CHARIOT so as to develop machine learning algorithms including variable selection, evolutionary optimisation, 
intelligent model identification and model validation. Together with IRIS, EBOS will contribute to the monitoring 
approach of the catalytic conversio n process by developing advanced data visualisation  and data analytics 
techniques, including data fusion strategies for maximising the information quality obtained from the different 
instrumentation and monitoring devices. Together with UOULU, EBOS will al so investigate Machine learning 
(ML) techniques for establishing a decision support system based on rule induction and case -based reasoning 
strategies for predictive maintenance and optimization in terms of energy - and material efficiency. In addition, 
Analytics Prediction models will be created by EBOS and presented through an interactive dashboard, highlighting 
out-of-bounds behaviors; identifying risk areas and alerting users in view of taking proactive maintenance actions. 
The advanced intelligence dash board will be used for both understanding processes and for post data analytical 
purposes to assist in the refinement and improvements of their performance. 
 
As part of WP5 ‘Validation, Process Simulation & Integration ’, EBOS will be involved in the s imulation and 
analysis of the existing and improved biorefinery processes which is focused on assessing and improving the 
overall performance of the BioSPRINT Process Intensification enhanced biorefinery concept. EBOS will work at 
the validation of the tools developed as part of WP2. 
 
Under WP6 ‘Integrated Lifecycle Sustainability Assessment’, EBOS will contribute in the Techno-economic 
assessment with modelling techniques and tools, leveraging advanced data analytics and data visualisation 
techniques which can support decision-making, for example related to investment. 
 
Moreover, EBOS will actively participate in the dissemination and communication activities of the project under 
WP7 ‘Dissemination and Exploitation’. EBOS' Creativity department will undertake the project’s identity and 
website design as part of Task 7.1 ‘Multidimensional dissemination, communication and stakeholder engagement 
activities’. EBOS will also design and create the project’s communication materials. In addition, as part of WP7, 
EBOS will contribute to the development and implementation in the Training, Education & Capacity Building 
programme (TECBP) , in particular EBOS will support the development of the online TECBP modules with 
appropriate and highly efficient ICT tools. 
 
Leveraging more than 15 years of experience in successfully developing and commercialising innovative 
solutions, as well as participating in EU-funded research projects, EBOS will undertake the role of Quality & Risk 
Management. As a leader of Task 8.3 Quality Assurance & Risk Management  under WP8 ‘Project 
Coordination’, EBOS will have the responsibility of organising and supervising quality review/peer reviews for 
all deliverables including the implementation of the qualit y management plan. EBOS will be also in charge of 
performing project quality evaluation criteria, risk assessment, continuous monitoring, triggering quality assurance 
project reviews, risk assessment procedures, evaluation measurements and producing risk a nd quality review 
reports. 
 
As part of WP8, EBOS will also support MAT in identifying and managing innovation from the project. In 
particular EBOS will be responsible for preparing and monitoring the implementation of the Data Management 
Plan (DMP), determ ining how innovation and research data are handled during and after the project, the 
application of the data privacy and pseudo -anonymisation techniques, privacy preserving data mining, security 
and consent management which will be applied to data collected in the project.

4.1.5 FRAUNHOFER GESELLSCHAFT ZUR FOERDERUNG DER ANGEWANDTEN FORSCHUNG E.V. 
Short Name FhG 
 
Country Germany 
Type Non-governmental organisation 
Website www.fraunhofer.de/ 
Short Profile 
The FRAUNHOFER GESELLSCHAFT ZUR FOERDERUNG DER ANGEWANDTEN FORSCHUNG E.V.  
(FhG) is the leading organi sation for applied research in Europe. Its research activities are conducted by 72 
institutes and research units at locations throughout Germany. FhG employs more than 25,000 of people who work 
with an annual research budget  of 2.3 bn euros  in total . Of th is sum, almost 2 bn euros are generated through 
contract research. Around 70% of the FhG’s contract research revenue is derived from contracts with industry and 
from publicly financed research projects. International collaborations with excellent research partners and 
innovative companies around the world ensure direct access to regions of the greatest importance to present and 
future scientific progress and economic development. 
The Fraunhofer Institute for Interfacial Engineering and Biotechnology (IGB) develops and optimizes processes, 
products and technologies in the business fields of health, chemistry and process industry, as well as environment 
and energy. IGB combines the highest scientific standards with professional know -how in competence areas – 
always with a view to economic efficiency and sustainability. Their competences comprise Interfacial Engineering 
and Materials Science, Molecular Biotechnology, Physical Process Technology, Environmental Biotechnology 
and Bioprocess Engineering, as well as Cell and Tissue Engineering. They offer solutions from market analysis 
through research & development till the finished product. 
In view of the finite nature of fossil resources, the growing demand for resources and climate change, the use of 
renewable raw materials has acquired great significance. The Fraunhofer Center for Chemical-Biotechnological 
Processes (CBP) in Leuna focuses on the combination of biotechnological processes with chemical processes, and 
with its pilot scale technical equipment it closes the gap between the laboratory and industrial implementation. By 
providing the infrastructure and technical facilities as well as a staff of highly qualified experts, it enables partners 
from research and industry to develop and scale up processes for th e utilization of renewable and petrochemical 
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 89 
 
raw materials to production-relevant dimensions, and also to accelerate process developments. Focus is laid on the 
use of vegetable oils, the disintegration of lignocelluloses and the production of technical enzymes. 
Role in the project 
FhG role in the project focuses on three dimensions: 
1. Production and provision of sample quantities (100 Liter Scale) of hemicellulose from the Organosolv process, 
directly from the pilot plants of Fraunhofer Center for Chemical-Biotechnological Processes (CBP).  
2. Implementation and scaling of chemical (via HTP, oxidation etc.) and biotechnological (e.g. by enzymatic 
conversion) conversion of hemicellulose -containing material streams (C5 and C6 sugars and its oligomers)  to 
furan derivatives;  
3. Purification of hemicellulose streams to isolate C5 and C6 sugars; separation and purification of furan 
derivatives, phenols from reaction mixtures, process development and scale up, process simulation 
 
In WP1 ‘Intensification of Upstream Purification’, FhG will be involved in the analysis of treated hemicellulose 
streams supplying an Organosolv stream from a pulping of beech wood pilot plant in order to perform the analysis 
of feedstocks. FhG will also be involved in the precipitation and solids handling by using dilution and distillation 
precipitation processes  so as to b enchmark tests . With support from UOULU,  FhG will focus on membrane 
purification as an intrinsically intensified separation technology. FhG will also support the optimisation of water 
and solvent recovery and reuse processes, which will be investigated using membrane distillation processes. 
 
Under WP3 ‘Intensification of Downstream Purification’ , FhG will lead the task relating to the p reparatory 
processing actions for downstream . In particular FhG will be in charge of the p rocess design simulation of 
distillation developing distillation simulation models and will also implement the 1st set of downstream separation 
experiments, separating primarily furans/5 -HMF from the extractive -reaction solvent.  In addition, FhG will 
participate in the Intensification of downstream purification processes , focusing on h eat transfer intensification 
with integration.  
 
As part of WP5 ‘Validation, Process Simulation & Integration’, FhG will take part in the simulation and analysis 
of the existing and improved biorefinery processes for the FhG Organosolv biorefining process and the information 
necessary to model the biorefinery process as close as possible to the  FhG facilities under study, and enable the 
KPI measurements and performance analysis. Thus, FhG will lead the integration of the developed concepts and 
technologies for the Organosolv stream with an emphasis on the validation of reaction and downstream purification 
technologies. Upon completion, a technology -transfer report will be produced indicating the prospect of 
integrating the realised intensified process into FhG biorefining operations. 
 
In WP7 ‘Dissemination  and Exploitation’ , FhG will support the Coordinator in the Multidimensional 
dissemination, communication and stakeholder engagement activities in order to develop the project’s 
multidimensional dissemination & communication (D&C) plan. 
 
FhG will lead the following tasks: 
− T3.1 Preparatory processing actions for downstream  
− T5.3 Integration of the developed concepts and technologies for Organosolv stream (FhG) 
 
FhG will take part in the tasks listed below: 
− T1.1 Analysis of treated hemicellulose streams 
− T1.2 Precipitation and solids handling 
− T1.3 Hybrid membrane purification and concentration of hemicellulose sugars 
− T1.5 Solvent and water recovery 
− T3.2 Development of distillation (with/w/o extraction)  
− T3.3 Intensification of Downstream Purification Processes  
− T5.1 Simulation and analysis of the existing and improved biorefinery processes  
− T7.1 Multidimensional dissemination, communication and stakeholder engagement activities
