Relevant Projects 
1. SteamBio [EU]: ‘Flexible Superheated Steam Torrefaction and Grinding of Indigenous Biomass from Remote 
Rural Sources to Produce Stable Densified Feedstocks for Chemical and Energy Applications’, The objective 
of SteamBio is to demonstrate a mobile processing concept that will enable efficient pre -treatment of agro-
forestry res idues for use as flexible feedstocks in chemical and process industries. These ligno -cellulosic 
materials originated from rural locations will be upgraded and densified into uniform sizes at source, allowing 
cost-effective transportation to existing industrial sites. (01/02/2015 – 31/07/2018), www.steambio.eu/. 
2. KomBiChemPRO [Other]: ‘Fine and platform chemicals from wood through combined chemical -
biotechnological processes’. As part of the joint project KombiChemPro, the results of various development 
work on the material use of renewable raw materials are to be brought together and combined with new 
approaches from research. These are to be demonstrated in an integrated concept, the process of which is both 
robust and efficient compared to conservatively produced platform chemicals.  The aim is to produce 
demanded, marketable products, which convince by a broad applicability and competitiveness against 
petrochemical manufactured platform chemicals. (01/10/2015 – 30/06/2019), funded by the Federal Ministry 
of Education and Research (BMBF). www.kombichempro.de/ 
3. Lignoplast [EU]: ‘Aromatic synthetic building blocks from lignin’. In the project both academic and industrial 
partners are working on processes to develop lignin as a source of raw materials for aromatic synthesis 
components. The required aromatic compounds are obtained by means of hydrolytic degradation of the 
macromolecular lignins and then functional ized chemically and enzymatically to make adhesives, paints, 
polyurethanes and epoxides. The lignin -based products are used in trial materials and subsequently 
characterized in terms of their application technology and compared with conventional systems. (01/03/2013 
–29/01/2016).www.igb.fraunhofer.de/en/research/competences/biocat/specialty-fine-
chemicals/lignoplast.html. 
4. ALIGN [Other]: ‘Aromatics from LIGNin’. ALIGN focuses on upscaling three extraction processes that lead 
to both a high-value lignin fraction and a pure cellulose/sugar fraction: The LX process (LXP), a Organosolv 
process combined with base-catalysed depolymerisation (BCD) and the lignin-first process (LFP). The lignin 
fractions derived from the three processes differ in their composition in regard to the degree of 
depolymerisation and functionalisation. Starting with this broad range of different lignin derivatives combined 
with tailor-made downstream processing (DSP) strategies, a wide variety of bio-based aromatics with unique 
properties can be produced. It aims at applying these bio-based aromatics as phenolic resins for the production 
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 91 
 
of high-pressure-laminates as well as natural vanillin for food and beverages. Funded by the Federal Ministry 
of Education and Research (BMBF). www.bigc-initiative.eu/align.php.  
Relevant Infrastructure 
FhG CBP is equipped with Lab scale, technical scale and pilot scale equipment for biomass pulping and raw 
material processing, conversion and isolation of value streams; TLR 3-6;  
Particularly relevant for the project:  
• Lignocellulose bio refinery namely pre -treatment and fractionation of lignocellulose biomass, proc ess 
engineering within chemical wood technology and analysis of lignocellulose composition and resulting  
process streams; 
• Development of chemical processes for the transformation of raw materials to basic and fine chemicals 
for reactions in gas and liquid phase or with solids, catalytic reactions under continuous and discontinuous 
conditions, reactions under high pressures (up to 350 bar) and temperatures  
(up to 500°C), simulation and modeling of processes and reaction units for process scaling, integrated 
process development and optimization (energy and resource efficiency), in-process analytics; 
• Development of processes for separation and purification of product mixtures; evaluation and 
development of methods for separation and purification, development of suitable methods and scale -up 
within different pilot plants, simulation and modelling of processes and integration of separation and 
purification steps in the overall process and evaluation of the whole value chain; 
• Feasibility studies for process development and evaluation, scale-up and optimization, concept and plant 
design as well as delivery of sample amounts (kg to t scale). 
 
4.1.6 IFEU - INSTITUT FUR ENERGIE UND UMWELTFORSCHUNG HEIDELBERG GMBH 
Short Name IFEU 
 
Country Germany 
Type Small or medium-size enterprise 
Website www.ifeu.de  
Short Profile 
Founded in 1978, the INSTITUT FÜR ENERGIE- UND UMWELTFORSCHUNG HEIDELBERG GMBH  - 
Institute for Energy and Environmental Research Heidelberg - (IFEU) conducts research and provides a worldwide 
consultancy service in relation to all major environmental and sustainability issues. With more than 40 years of 
experience, IFEU is one of the most important ecological research institutes in Germany. Currently, IFEU employs 
67 researchers consisting of specialists from all major fields of environmental sciences. In 2017, its annual turnover 
was €5.25 million. As an independent body for environmental research and consulting, IFEU has an extensi ve 
track record in areas such as waste management and packaging materials, transport & mobility, renewable energies 
and energy efficiency as well as food and bio-based systems.  
 
IFEU is especially renowned for its expertise (>25 years) in the field of Life Cycle Assessment (LCA) and 
Environmental Impact Assessment (EIA). Recently, IFEU developed the integrated life cycle sustainability 
assessment (ILCSA) methodology (see figure 1 below), and applied it successfully in dozens of projects in the last 
10 year s. IFEU executed more than 250 LCAs and sustainability assessments on existing and innovative 
technologies in the field of renewable energies and materials (notably bioenergy and bio -based 
materials/chemicals) starting more than 25 years ago.  
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 92 
 
 
Figure 1: Integrated Life Cycle Sustainability Assessment (ILCSA) 
IFEU has been working on the environmental impacts of biorefineries for the past years and evaluated dozens of 
biorefinery concepts for biodiesel, bioethanol and bio gas but also bio-based products. In recent years, a specific 
focus was put on lignocellulose biorefineries and algae biorefineries. In addition, IFEU has been working on the 
sustainability assessment of lignocellulosic biorefineries since the late 1990s, b efore the concept of second 
generation biofuels even existed, assessing the development of lignocellulosic biorefineries from the experimental 
stages to large -scale plants. IFEU’s expertise helps to optimise the process development from a sustainability 
perspective, and shows both the disadvantages and risks along with the advantages and opportunities associated 
with the different concepts. 
 
At European level, IFEU has been involved in a number of projects on lignocellulosic biomass such as BIOLYFE 
(GA No. 239204), BIOCORE (GA No. 241566), SUPRABIO (GA No. 241640) and OPTIMA (GA No. 289642). 
In all these projects, the IFEU department of ‘Food and bio-based systems’ has led the work package on integrated 
lifecycle sustainability assessment (ILCSA).  
 
The clients and sponsors of IFEU include governments, federal and federal -state ministries and associated 
authorities (e.g. the German Federal Environment Agency), the European Commission, national and international 
foundations, UN organizations (e.g. FAO, UNEP and UNFCCC), private enterprises, associations and 
environmental organizations. 
Role in the project 
IFEU will lead WP6 ‘Integrated Lifecycle Sustainability Assessment’ (organized as indicated in Figure 2 below) 
to assess the sustainability impacts of the BioSPRINT processes and products, including environmental and 
techno-economic benefits and risks. Thi s will be done based on process data obtained fro m the previous work 
packages, but also includes theoretical assumptions.

                                                                                                                                                                      Page 93 
 
 
 
Figure 2: BioSPRINT Integrated Sustainability Assessment 
 
In the d efinitions, settings and system description IFEU will contribute to the goal and scope definitions and 
settings for the sustainability assessment, which will be used by all subsequent Tasks (6.2 to 6.6) to guarantee a 
coherent analysis throughout the whole WP. First, the key questions to  be answered by the sustainability 
assessment will be defined.  
 
In addition, IFEU will be in charge of the Environmental Life Cycle Assessment (LCA)  so as to evaluate the 
environmental impacts associated with the targeted BioSPRINT products in comparison to all selected reference 
products. The Environmental Life cycle assessment (E-LCA) will address the environmental aspects and potential 
environmental impacts (e.g. use of resources, environmental consequences of emissions) of a product. A wide 
range of impact categories will be covered (e.g. climate change, ozone depletion, acidification, eutrophication and 
resource depletion), providing a comprehensive picture of the product’s environmental implications. The 
assessment includes the product’s entire life cycle from raw material acquisition through production, use, end-of 
life treatment, recycling and final disposal. 
 
IFEU will also be involved in the Socio-economic assessment in order to assess the s ocio-economic impact by 
measuring the contribution of the project to both economic and social well -being. IFEU will support MAT to 
explore whether there are any direct risks to society e.g. health, safety, economic and environmental security, 
posed by the implementation and uptake of BioSPRINT project and target products. 
 
IFEU with its great expertise in Integrated life cycle sustainability assessment will have the responsibility to check 
the results from the previous analyses (Tasks 6.2 to 6.5) are integrated to identify and depict the most sustainable 
pathways among the BioSPRINT value chains compared to all reference systems. IFEU will use a multi -criteria 
evaluation software tool following the innovative methodology of Integrated Life Cycle Sustainability Assessment 
(ILCSA) covering all sustainability indicators chosen. 
 
In WP7 ‘Dissemination and Exploitation’ , IFEU will take part in the m ultidimensional dissemination, 
communication and stakeholder engagement activities supporting DEC to develop the project’s multidimensional 
dissemination & communication (D&C) plan; deliver D&C activities.  
 
In WP8 ‘Project coordination’ IFEU will support the Project Coordinator DEC, in the overall coordination, 
management and reporting as WP6 leader.

Key Personnel 
Dr. Guido Reinhardt (Male) is the Scientific Director  of Institute for Energy and Environmental Research 
Heidelberg (IFEU), a member of the scientific board and scientific director of the department of ‘Sustainability of 
renewable energies and biobased system s’. Since he joined IFEU in 1991, he has been working in the fields of 
Life Cycle Assessment (LCA), transport and environment, environmental assessments of food, bioenergy, 
industrial crops, bio-based materials and algae. He has a broad experience in the a cquisition and coordination of 
large-scale projects and is a consultant for national and international institutions and a member of several advisory 
panels.  
 
Nils Rettenmaier (Male) is a Senior Scientist and Senior Project leader at IFEU. His main working fields are: life 
cycle inventories (LCI), biomass resource assessments and sustainability criteria. Nils is involved in several 
projects both at a  national and EU level and has led the work packages on sustainability assessment e.g. in 
BIOCORE, SUPRABIO and OPTIMA. He is member of several panels, e.g. the VDI (Association of German 
Engineers) guideline committee 6310 'Classification and quality criteria of biorefineries' and the CEN/TC 411/WG 
4 ‘Sustainability criteria, life cycle analysis and related issues’ and chairs the German Institute for Standardization 
(DIN) committee NA 17200-11 AA 'Bio-based products' (which mirrors CEN/TC 411) since January 2016.  Nils 
will be the Leader of WP6 ‘ Integrated Lifecycle Sustainability Assessment’ and serve as the Sustainability, 
Safety and Security Manager.  
 
Sven O. Gärtner, Dipl.-Phys. Ing., (Male) is a senior scientist and project leader at IFEU. Working at IFEU for 
more than 15 years, Sven Gärtner has  a wide experience in life cycle assessment (LCA), especially concerning 
biomass and food. Projects he has been involved in dealt with 1st and 2nd generation biofuels, biogas in its 
different usage forms, heat and power from woody and herbaceous biomass including perennial grasses as well as 
the material use of biomass for biochemicals in biorefinery approaches. In his department, he supervises the LCA 
calculations and the data management for life cycle inventories.  
 
Dr. Heiko Keller (Male) is a Senior Scientist and Project leader at IFEU. His main working fields are Life Cycle 
Assessment (LCA) and Integrated Sustainability Assessment (ILCSA), which covers environmental, social, 
economic and technological aspects of sustainability. Heiko is a scientific advisory member of the working group 
on sustainable wood energy of the German bioenergy association Bundesverband Bio-Energie e.V. (BBE). He is 
a visiting lecturer for Life Cycle Assessment at Karlsruhe Institute of Technology (KIT). 
 
Dominik Jessing (Male) is a Project Manager at IFEU. Dominik studied biology and public law at the University 
of Heidelberg. He is c urrently undergoing in-service training, Master studies in evaluation at the Centrum for 
Evaluation (CEval) at the University of the Saarland. He is a Member of the Society for Evaluation (DeGEval – 
Gesellschaft für Evaluation e.V.), and speaker of the Work Group ‘Environment’. He has been teaching for several 
at the Geography Institute of the University of Heidelbe rg. Dominik will serve as the Data Protection Officer of 
IFEU.

Relevant projects 
1. UNRAVEL [EU]: ‘UNique Refinery Approach to Valorise European Lignocellulosics’. UNRAVEL aims to 
develop advanced pre-treatment, separation and conversion technologies for complex lignocellulosic biomass 
to produce usable lignin fragments, and monomeric sugars fro m the cellulose and hemicellulose fraction 
suitable for biochemical conversions. BBI project (BBI -792004, 2018 -2022). IFEU is leading the WP on 
sustainability assessment. TNO’s FABIOLA™ low temperature, energy-efficient acetone based fractionation 
process will be assessed. (01/06/2018 – 31/05/2022). www.unravel-bbi.eu/.  
2. BIOLYFE [EU]: Second generation BIOethanol process: demonstration scale for the step of Lignocellulosic 
hYdrolysis and FErmentation. The focus of this project was on lignocellulose pre -treatment via steam 
explosion and simultaneous saccharification and co -fermentation (SScF) of cellulose and hemicellulose into 
ethanol (FP7 -239204, 2010 -2013). IFEU was a subcontractor to IUS and led  the WP on Sustainability 
assessment. In particular, IFEU was involved in the Integrated sustainabi lity assessment. The study 
demonstrated how established assessment methodologies such as environmental LCA and cost benefit analysis 
from a business perspective can be supplemented by innovative approaches to cover and integrate all 
sustainability related aspects of future BIOLYFE biorefineries. IFEU contributed in  the integrated 
sustainability evaluation which was also performed as part of this project. It aimed to analyse whether future, 
large-scale dissemination of the PROESA™ technology provides benefits from environmental, economic and 
social perspectives compared to the use of existing biofuels or fossil fuels. This comprehensive analysis 
investigated scenarios on future implementation of this technology, from the provision of raw materials to the 
energy utilisation of the bioethanol, and a variety of optimisation options.  (01/01/2010 – 31/12/2013). 
www.biolyfe.eu/.  
3. SUPRABIO [EU]: ‘Sustainable products from economic processing of biomass in highly integrated 
biorefineries’. The biochemical routes investigated in this project were also based on lignocellulose pre -
treatment via steam explosion and simultaneous saccharification and co-fermentation (SScF) of cellulose and 
hemicellulose into ethanol (FP7-241640, 2010-2014). IFEU led the WP on sustainability assessment. Danish 
company BioGasol’s biomass fractionation technology was analysed. (01/02/2010 – 31/07/2014). 
www.suprabio.eu/.  
4. BIOCORE [EU]: ‘BIOCOmmodity Refinery’. BIOCORE  creates and demonstrates a lignocellulosic 
biorefinery for sustainable processing of agricultural residues (wheat and rice straws), SRC wood (poplar) and 
hardwood forestry residues, into 2G biofuels, bulk chemicals, polymers, speciality molecules, heat and power 
(FP7-241566, 2010-2014). IFEU led the WP on sustainability assessment. Biorefining of straws and wood 
into specialty polymers, fuels, and materials was the main focus of this project which was based on an 
Organosolv pretreatment by French company CIMV. (01/03/2010 – 28/02/2014). www.biocore-europe.org/.  
5. OPTIMA: Optimization of Perennial Grasses for Biomass Production, (FP7 -289642, 2011-2015). IFEU led 
the WP on sustainability assessment. The integrated  sustainability assessment covered the conversion of 
lignocellulosic biomass from marginal land into ethanol. (01/10/2011 – 30/09/2015) 
cordis.europa.eu/project/rcn/101188/factsheet/en

4.1.7 IRIS TECHNOLOGY SOLUTIONS, SOCIEDAD LIMITADA 
Short Name IRIS 
 
Country Spain 
Type Small or medium-size enterprise 
Website www.iristechnologygroup.com/ 
Short Profile 
IRIS TECHNOLOGY SOLUTIONS, SOCIEDAD LIMITADA (IRIS) is an advanced engineering company 
established in Barcelona in 2007 with a mission of bringing process optimisation solutions to manufacturing. IRIS 
focuses on Key Enabling Technologies for Digital Transformation: making Industry smarter, more sustainable and 
efficient in Industry 4.0. Currently the company employs 60+ staff with a turnover of €5m. It is equipped with 
three engineering workshops, food testing and wet chemistry laboratory, two optics labs, and an 
electronics/telecommunications lab. 
  
IRIS specialises in the manufacture and integration of Process Analytical Technology (PAT) -based real -time 
quality monitoring solutions for the process industries and IoT systems for smart manufacturing, predominantly 
targeted at the food, pharmaceutical and chemical industries. In particular, IRIS product line comprises proprietary 
state-of-the-art infrared analyzers for at-line and in-line process monitoring.  
 
On the one hand IRIS solutions are based on the latest developments in photonics -in the fields of Near Infrared 
Spectroscopy, Hyperspectral Imaging, and Raman Spectroscopy. On the other hand, IRIS leverages ICTs, whereby 
they apply Machine learning, Artificial Intelligence and Data Mining techniques for predictive and active control, 
as well as for decision support systems. In addition to photonics-based analyzers, IRIS’s staff also works with IoT 
sensors for enabling equipment and machinery for smart manufacturing and transitioning industry to the 
Industry4.0 paradigm. IRIS solutions are cloud-based for mobility, remote monitoring and multi-site applications.  
The company’s Innovation Division which is governed by an Innovation Committee comprising Senior 
Management, and an Innovation Unit for managing and executing the company’s innovation roadmap, has three 
core strategic lines, for shaping the Factory of the Future: 
− Circular and Bio-based Economy: digitalization and waste valorization; 
− New optical photonics-based technologies and PAT systems for production process optimization; 
− ICTs (Artificial intelligence / machine learning, IOT & cloud platforms). 
 
In addition to running an internal R&D programme, as well as carrying various joint private projects with industry 
partners, the Innovation Division is highly experienced in working in collaborative R&D projects in H2020 (both 
as coordinators and partners), and principally in the SPIRE, FoF, and BBI programmes. Thanks to the expertise 
obtained in R&D projects, IRIS designed and developed its own devices based on Infrared Spectroscopy, with the 
mission of integrating novel inline monitoring systems for quality improvement and process standardisation in the 
food, pharmaceutical and chemical industries, among others. As such, in 2016, the VISUM brand was born. The 
Value Proposition for the in dustry of VISUM is to bring affordable and reliable laboratory analytical capability 
into manufacturing lines (Lab2Line) and right along the value chain (Lab2Chain) for real-time process monitoring 
and quality inspection purposes.     
 
IRIS is ISO 9001:200 8 certified and also is certified under UNE -EN-ISO 166002: Management Systems R&D. 
IRIS is also certified by the local (Catalonian) government as a provider of technological R&D services (Tecnio 
Certification).  
 
IRIS is a member of the following sectorial  networks: SPIE and SECPHO, in addition to regional industrial 
collectives such as Smart Space (association of companies and organisations that specialise in the ‘smartification’ 
of industry). In addition, IRIS is a member of A.SPIRE, the European Association which is committed to manage 
and implement the SPIRE Public-Private Partnership. 
Role in the project 
IRIS role in the project will be focused on: 
1) Development of monitoring and control strategies for bio-based processes by applying IRIS background 
on PAT solutions;  
2) Support to IT developments in particular related to Machine Learning. 
3) Application of ultrasounds technology as possible pre-treatment stage.

In WP1 ‘Intensification of Upstream Purification’, IRIS will lead the activities on the identification of upstream 
scale-up challenges via process systems engineering (PSE) tools  in order to generate experimental data for the 
validation of the process system engineering tools. Similarly, in WP4 ‘Development of Biorenewable Resins and 
Polymerisation Intensification’, IRIS will lead the activities on the i dentification of polymerisation scale -up 
challenges via process systems engineering tools. The polymerisation processes intensified in this WP is analysed 
using CFD tools at lab-scale. IRIS effort aims to provide a certain set of recommendations on how to scale-up an 
intensified polymerisation reactor. These recommendations will include the thermo-fluid behaviour of the reactor 
using CFD tools, the control analysis and PAT techniques on the later-on pilot plant equipment. 
 
In WP2 ‘Intensification of Catalytic Conversion’, IRIS will support ADSC in the identification of reaction scale-
up challenges via process systems engineering tools , whereas as part of WP3 ‘Intensification of Downstream 
Purification’, IRIS will support UOULU in the i dentification of downstream scale -up challenges in the 
downstream purification processes, which have been analysed using the CFD tools at lab scale opera tion. IRIS 
background on PAT solutions and techniques will provide the results that will be used to identify scale-up. 
 
In WP5 ‘Validation, Process Simulation & Integration’, IRIS will support UPM on the integration of upstream, 
reaction and downstream pro cesses. In addition, IRIS will participate in the s cale-up of optimal product 
formulations. 
 
Under WP7 ‘Dissemination and Exploitation’, IRIS will support the Project Coordinator to develop the project’s 
multidimensional dissemination & communication (D&C) plan , deliver D&C activities . Moreover, IRIS will 
primarily assist MAT to survey the broader market with a view to assessing sectoral needs, considering how other 
actors are responding.  
 
IRIS will lead the following tasks: 
− T1.4 Identification of upstream scale-up challenges via process systems engineering (PSE) tools 
− T4.5 Identification of polymerisation scale-up challenges via process systems engineering tools 
 
IRIS will take part in the tasks listed below: 
− T2.4 Identification of reaction scale-up challenges via process systems engineering tools 
− T3.4 Identification of downstream scale-up challenges 
− T5.2 Integration of the developed concepts and technologies for UPM stream 
− T5.5 Scale-up of optimal product formulations 
− T7.1 Multidimensional dissemination, communication and stakeholder engagement activities 
− T7.3 Identification of early adopters, post-project opportunities and business plan

Relevant Projects 
1. AgriMax [EU]: ‘Agri and food waste valorisation co -ops based on flexible multi -feedstocks biorefinery 
processing technologies for new high added value applications’. To extract the significant amounts of valuable 
compounds contained in these wastes, AgriMax will combine affordable and flexible processing technologies 
(ultrasound assisted and solvent extraction, filtration, thermal and enzymatic treatments) for the valo rization 
of side streams from the horticultural culture and food processing industry to be used in a cooperative approach 
by local stakeholders. (01/10/2016 – 30/09/2020). www.agrimax-project.eu/.  
2. IbD [EU]: “ Intensified by Design® for the intensification of processes involving solids handling" IbD® 
Project has created a holistic platform for facilitating process intensification design and optimisation in 
processes in which solids are an intrinsic part across t he ceramic processing, pharmaceutical, chemical, 
mineral and ore processing sectors.” (01/09/2015-31/08/2018). www.ibd-project.eu/  
3. BIOnTOP [EU]: ‘Novel packaging films and textiles with tailored end of life and performance based on bio-
based copolymers and coatings ’. The BIOnTOP project will deliver recyclable -by-design cost competitive 
packaging solutions that can be mechanically recycled, industrially/home composted or even suitable for 
anaerobic digestion. (01/06/2019 – 31/05/2023). Website under construction.  
4. URBIOFIN [EU] Demonstration of an integrated innovative biorefinery for the transformation of Municipal 
Solid Waste (MSW) into new BioBased products. The aim of URBIOFIN project is to demonstrate the techno-
economic and environmental viability of the conversion at semi-industrial scale (10 T/d) of the organic fraction 
of MSW (OFMSW) into: Chemical building blocks (bioethanol, volatile fatty acids, biogas), biopolymers 
(polyhydroyalkanoate and biocomposites) or additives (microalgae hydrolisated for biofertilisers). By u sing 
the biorefinery concept applied to MSW (urban biorefinery), URBIOFIN will exploit the OFMSW as 
feedstock to produce different valuable marketable products for different markets: agriculture, cosmetics.  
(01/06/2017 – 31/12/2021). www.urbiofin.eu/ This project is under VISUM Ltd, the Irish branch under IRIS 
Technology Group. 
5. PERCAL [EU] Chemical building blocks from versatile MSW biorefinery. PERCAL will exploit Municipal 
Solid Waste (MSW) as feedstock to develop i ntermediate chemical products at high yield and low impurity 
level with huge industrial interest. These will be complementary to the bioethanol (current PERSEO 
technology), to achieve a cascade valorisation of the MSW components . (01/07/2017 – 30/06/2020). 
www.percal-project.eu/. This project is under VISUM Ltd, the Irish branch under IRIS Technology Group.

4.1.8 KEMIJSKI INSTITUT 
Short Name NIC 
 
Country Slovenia 
Type Research Organisation 
Website www.ki.si/en/ 
Short Profile 
The National Institute of Chemistry, Ljubljana, Slovenia (NIC), is a leading Slovenian research institution in the 
field of chemistry and related scientific disciplines. Basic and applied research are oriented towards fields which 
are of long -term importance to both Slovenia and the world: materials research, life sciences, biotechnology, 
chemical engineering, structural and theoretical chemistry, analytical chemistry and environmental protection; 
through which the institute is in line with the needs of the  domestic and foreign pharmaceutical, chemical, 
automotive and nanobiotechnological industries. 
 
The work of the Institute is also in line with the priority thematic areas of the EU Research and Innovation 
programme Horizon 2020, which places an emphasis on nanotechnology, genomics and biotechnology for health, 
climate change, energy, sustainable development and global change and quality and safety of food. 
 
The National Institute of Chemistry has 331 employees (31.3.2019), of which around 292 carry out research work 
in 9 departments and two infrastructure centers; 149 of these have doctorates of science degrees. 
 
NIC’s fields of activity are listed below: 
- Research, particularly related to Process Intensification, Catalysis, Biochemistry, Chemical Reaction 
Engineering, Energy management and efficiency, etc. 
- Education: Currently 74 graduate students are being trained at the Institute within the national Young 
Researchers Program for the acquisition of their PhD degrees. The young researchers represent about 25% 
of the Institute's staff members, making National Institute of Chemistry one of the leading Slovenian 
organizations for graduate-level education and training. 
- Cooperation with industry : Research is oriented towards the development of new techno logies and 
products, which will help to ensure the long-term development of Slovenia and which are internationally 
relevant. Industry is an important partner to the Institute in these endeavors. There are a number of 
Slovenian companies with whom the Insti tute has entered into close long -term cooperation, as well as a 
number of well -regarded foreign companies. From a financial point of view, this kind of cooperation 
represents 20% of the income of the Institute. 
 
The Institute offers high-level research equipment, allowing researchers to engage in even the most cutting edge 
research challenges at the world level. 
 
NIC will involve the Department of Catalysis and Chemical Reaction Engineering which is primarily invested in 
chemical (process) engineering, reactor and unit operation design and construction, as well as multi-scale process 
modelling. The Department topics foremost include carbon dioxide and natural gas conversion, hydrogen and fuel 
cell technologies, biomass valorisation to bio-based compounds, and (bio)pharmaceutical processes. 
 
The National Institute of Chemistry is 1 of the 3 original founding partners of the Slovenian Strategic Resear ch 
and Innovation Partnership (SRIP) Networks for the Transition into Circular Economy , which is a cluster -like 
national stakeholder in the field of circular economy implementation.  Moreover, NIC is a member of SusChem, 
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 101 
 
the European Technology Platform for Sustainable Chemistry. SusChem National Technology Platform Slovenia 
(NTP Slovenia) is lead by NIC. NTP Slovenia is one of the 17 National Technology Platforms of Su sChem’s 
network of national platforms which are considered k ey to the involvement of national stakeholders including 
small and medium -sized enterprises (SMEs), large companies and academic groups, in European initiatives  
relating to, among others, biotechn ology, advanced materials, new & improved processes and clean sustainable 
technologies. 
Via its membership in the ‘Chamber of Commerce and Industry of Stajerska’, Slovenia , NIC  is a n associate 
member of the BIC consortium, the European Association which represents the private sector in the Bio-based 
Industries Joint Undertaking (BBI JU). 
Role in the project 
NIC’s role in BioSPRINT is focused on: 
1) Process intensification, in particular of catalytic conversion, downstream purification and polymerisation 
reactions, in view of achieving intensified and integrated final processes, as well as the intensification of 
these unit operations. This is directly related to extensive background knowledge in chemical reactor 
engineering, as well as specific (bio-economy) patent applications. NIC will intensify, optimize and scale-
up the production of bio-based furans, as well as hydroxyl-methyl-furfural, (targeted) intermediate. 
2) The strategic planning, delivery and evaluation of an impact Training, Education and Capacity -Building 
Programme (TECBP) aiming at maximising the potential for BioSPRINT’s results to be leveraged by 
actors beyond the consortium. 
 
In WP1 ‘Intensification of Upstream Purification’ , NIC will undertake the analysis of treated hemicellulose 
streams which will be supplied by FhG, UPM and Clariant and serve as a foundation for further technical work in 
the project . NIC will thus provide r eports on feedstock variability analysis collecting immediate upstream 
implications.  
 
As part of WP2 ‘Intensification of Catalytic Conversion’, NIC will take part in the c atalyst Development using 
HTP Methods to deliver robust catalyst formulations for integrated conversion of C5 and C6 sugars into a single 
reactor, coupled with extraction of reactive furan intermediated. Additionally, NIC will monitor the reactions for 
realistic stream mixtures. In particular, NIC will be in charge of the chemical kinetics determination, modelling & 
simulations which will be evaluated for synthetic, as well as for realistic feedstock mixtures ; the integration of 
synthetic sugar mixtures which will be applied before proceeding to realistic feedstock compositions in order to 
individually establish the interactions between the former, at first excluding the influences of impurities from, e.g. 
lignin. Moreover, NIC will contribute in the development of extractive reaction intensification being responsible 
for the application/extensio n of the modelling from the purely reactive mechanisms to intensified reaction –
extraction operation. 
 
NIC will be the Leader of WP3 ‘Intensification of Downstream Purification’. In particular, NIC’s involvement 
will be focused on the following: in the p reparatory processing actions for downstream NIC will be in charge of 
the reaction composition analysis for downstream especially for the exact composition determination. Moreover, 
NIC will monitor the development of distillation focusing on the modelling validation, simulation and optimisation 
to be executed in order to expand the range of conditions, compositions and purities to be predicted by simulations. 
As a result, NIC will provide the modelling of distillation to support the scale-up of pilot unit operation. The scale-
up to the TRL 4–5 operation will be the responsibility of FhG, as factors, such as fluidics, monitoring and control 
will be considered. NIC will start the pilot scale validation based on multi-scale modelling simulations which will 
be implemented and finalised by FhG. NIC will be in addition involved in the i ntensification of downstream 
purification will be focused in the reduction in foot print and hazardous inventory for the liquid-liquid decanter 
unit that separates the aqueous and organic phases originating from the extractive-reaction unit.  
 
In WP4 ‘Development of Biorenewable Resins and Polymerisation Intensification’ , NIC will support AEP on 
the development and testing of novolac-type resins and bio-based polyols in order to intensify the processes for 
the production of resins and polyols and support the task related to the intensification of polymerisation processes. 
 
Under WP5 ‘Validation, Process Simulation & Integration’, NIC will contribute to the integration of  the 
developed concepts and technologies for the UPM stream and the FhG Organosolv streams  and also assist DEC 
to perform a transferability and replicability case study using the stream of associated partner Clariant.  
 
In WP7 ‘Dissemination and Exploitation’ , NIC will participate in the dissemination and communication 
activities. In addition, NIC will lead the Training, Education & Capacity Building programme (TECBP) with 
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.

the participation of academic,  research and industrial partners . Materials will be developed in line with best

NIC, together with the  rest Work packages  leaders and EBOS, w ill develop, implement and deliver 4 online

As part of WP8 ‘Project coordination’, NIC will assist the project Coordinator (DEC) in the overall project

Key Personnel 
Prof. Dr. Blaž Likozar (Male) is the Head of the Department of Catalysis and Chemical Reaction Engineering at 
the National Institute of Chemistry  (NIC). Dr. Blaž earned his PhD in Chemical Engineering in 2008 from the 
University of Ljubljana. He has been working at NIC for 7 years as the Head of department, as well as Senior 
research fellow and Assistant Professor in the field of chemical engineering . He is responsible for (leading) the 
programme “Chemical Reaction Engineering” as well as several research projects. His expertise lies  in 
heterogeneous catalyst materials, modelling, simulation and optimization of process fluid mechanics, transport 
phenomena and chemical kinetics. Between 2014–2015 he worked at the University of Delaware (Catalysis Center 
for Energy Innovation, Newark, Delaware, USA), as a Fulbright Visiting Scholar Program researcher in the field 
of chemical engineering. Prof. Likozar has published over 120 original peer-reviewed scientific research papers 
and has the h-index of 19 (presently, 1477 citations). He has expertise in, in terms of scientific category keywords, 
chemical engineering, reaction engineering, reactor engineering, heterogeneous catalysis, process optimisation, 
process int ensification, valorisation, multi -scale modelling, density functional theory, kinetic Monte Carlo, 
computational fluid dynamics, thermodynamics, reaction kinetics, micro -kinetics, transport phenomena, heat 
transfer, mass transfer, fluid mechanics, unit ope rations, and separations. He is a co -author of numerous patent 
applications, e.g. Process and related system for removing ashes from biomasses, 2016. In 2018, he received the 
Prometheus of Science for Excellence in Communication. Since, 2017, he is a membe r of the Working Party on 
Chemical Reaction Engineering and also the Program board vice president of Strategic Research and Innovation 
Partnership (SRIP) Networks for the transition into circular economy . Since, 2016, he is the NIC’s EERA 
Bioenergy representative. He is the WP leader in 5 H2020 projects in MefCO2,  ADREM, FReSMe, BiZeolCat 
and ReaxPro. Since 2016, he is also the project leader in the programme CEL.CYCLE. Dr. Blaz is also the 
President of SusChem Slovenia. Blaz will serve as the Capacity Building Manager.

and PhD in 2015 at the University of Ljubljana, Faculty of Chemistry and Chemical Technology. He was awarded

4.1.9 MATURUS OPTIMI BV 
Short Name MAT 
 
Country Netherlands 
Type Small to Medium sized Enterprise 
Website www.maturusoptimi.com 
Short Profile 
Maturus Optimi bv  (MAT) is a n  engineering and strategic consultancy focusing on process design, energy 
efficiency, sustainability and techno-economic feasibility of new and existing industrial processes serving a variety 
of research, technology, engineering and manufacturing organisations across different industrial sector s, such as 
Chemicals, Oil & Gas, Mining, Renewables, Biotech, Biobased, Pharmaceuticals, and Life Science. 
 
MAT applies extensive expert knowledge along with industry standards and inhouse developed tools to support 
process development and scale up activit ies and to deliver cost -effective plant designs. MAT solutions entail: 
detailed and first principle unit operation modelling, dynamic and steady state process simulation, process energy 
analysis, heat and process integration, process equipment design, capital cost estimation, financial assessment and 
risk analysis (Monte Carlo based simulation). MAT areas of expertise include: 
− Process Engineering: dealing with any process engineering challenge in Front End Design (new processes 
and technologies) as well as in Running Plants. With respect to Front End Design, MAT specializes in 
converting new technologies and new process ideas into fully developed process concepts. This 
specifically includes: deriving model -based mass and energy balances, drafting process alternatives, 
optimization, preliminary designs, etc. Furthermore, they identify steps and resources that are necessary 
to complete such tasks. Th is expertise is of great importance to organizations that need to evaluate 
innovative ideas and develop new businesses or products. For Running Plants, MAT offers solutions that 
support plant operation and manufacturing in improving their daily activities.  Most commonly these 
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 105 
 
solutions are focused on providing plant staff with model-based advice on process operation and control. 
These so-called decision-making tools are exceptionally effective for improving plant efficiency up to 5% 
or more.   
− Cost Estimating and Process Economics: providing customers with complete business cases, containing 
the economic data related to the project, from capital costs until operational costs. Evaluations are carried 
out for all scenarios whether new or existing plants, full or partial processes. MAT solutions include 
complete economic evaluation with recommendations and risks. In this way, MAT provides guidance to 
R&D and speed up towards a successful project. 
− Socio Economic Assessment:  MAT assesses the economic and social impact which projects have on the 
community and businesses on a larger scale and in the longer run. The impacts are measured by the 
economic and social well -being parameters such as job and value creation, quality of life, health and 
security. MAT helps harness the information to develop a business case for action and make strategic 
recommendations to maximise impact.  
− Energy Efficiency: combining sophisticated modelling tools, various energy analysis methodologies and 
rich industrial experience, MAT provides solutions that meet clients’ energy challenges. For existing plant 
facilities MAT focuses on: evaluating the current status of process energy efficiency, identifying energy 
savings opportunities and recommending energy effective designs and solutions. Depending on different 
factors such as the age, design and adaptability of a plant, MAT’s solutions bring from 3% to over 20% 
in energy efficiency increase. This ultimately results in: reducing the production costs, reducing carbon 
emissions and increasing the product value. Regarding new processes, MAT helps its customers to focus 
on technology selection and design that is led by energy efficient solutions. 
 
MAT has participated in many industrial projects related to process development, design and techno-economic 
optimization studies supporting R&D of many large organizations from various industrial sectors through the 
process of selection and development of new and unproven technologies. Furthermore, MAT has conducted a 
number of research studi es related to improving manufacturing performance through retrofit of the existing and 
the implementation of new technologies.  
 
MAT has extensive experience with the application of the industry standard, state of the art software AspenTech 
to perform techno-economic modelling and simulation of industrial processes.  
 
MAT network of partners includes : DSM, DuPont, Invista, LanzaTech, CPI UK, Ioniqa, Lanxess, Maire 
Tecnimont, Farabi Petrochemical Company, Energie Beheer Nederland (EBN), ECN Netherlands. 
Role in the project 
MAT will be responsible for leading techno -economic and socio -economic assessment studies in Bio SPRINT 
project. The goal is to analyze and evaluate, early on, technological feasibility and economic viability of the 
BioSPRINT solutions for the existing and new biorefineries. MAT identifies limitations, risks and opportunities 
related to the implementation of the new technology, allowing the project to better focus the research and optimize 
the process design at the early phase of the project. 
 
In WP5 ‘Validation, Process Simulation & Integration’, MAT will lead the task on the s imulation and analysis 
of the existing and improved biorefinery processes . In particular, MAT will be responsible to define  biorefinery 
process boundaries & collect data . MAT will describe standard biorefinery process  in terms of technology, 
products, wastes stream, process conditions and energy consumption. Process boundaries will be setup to include 
key technological steps relevant for BioSPRINT. Physical properties data will be collected for nonconventional 
compounds. MAT will source data from literature and its own database, as well as relevant information provided 
by industrial partners UPM and FhG . MAT will use  these data and information in order to build a simulation 
model of the baseline biorefinery and validate this using state-of-the-art industry standard software tool AspenPlus. 
As part of WP5, MAT will also support UPM, FhG and DEC to integrate the developed concepts and technologies 
for the UPM stream and the FhG Organosolv streams;  and perform a transferability and replicability case study 
using the stream of associated partner Clariant.  
 
Under WP6 ‘Integrated Lifecycle Sustainability Assessment’ , MAT will contribute in the definitions, settings 
and system description. MAT will be responsible for the techno-economic and socio-economic assessment. MAT 
will develop e conomic models of the improved biorefinery, with P rocess Intensification (PI)  technologies 
implemented, in the state-of-the-art software tool Aspen Process Economic Analyzer. MAT will assess the socio-
economic impact by measuring the contribution of the project to both economic and social well-being and whether

                                                                                                                                                                      Page 106 
 
there are any direct risks to society e.g. health, safety, economic and environmental security, posed by the 
implementation and uptake of BioSPRINT project and target products. 
 
In WP7 ‘Dissemination and Exploitation’, MAT will take part in the dissemination and communication activities. 
In addition, MAT will be responsible for the identification of early adopters and post-project opportunities as well 
as the development of a business plan. In particular, MAT will survey the broader market with a view to assessing 
sectoral needs, considering how other actors are responding to the problem in this space.  
 
As part of WP8 ‘Project coordination’, MAT will support the project Coordinator in the overall coordination , 
reporting and management of the project. Moreover, MAT will undertake the role of Innovation, IPR & Data 
Management. MAT, supported by EBOS, will identify and manage innovation from the project, advising the 
Project Manager and partners on the scope and potential of the innovations arising and paying attention to 
discerning IPR at regular checkpoints. Work includes the monitoring of the progress of development of innovative 
tools/services throughout the project. In order t o ensure sustainability, exploitation and marketability of the 
project’s results, MAT will design the IPR protection strategy, and establish IPR management procedures and 
associated activities. All IP produced is monitored and the potential IPR attached to them (e.g. copyright, patent, 
etc.) are verified and cleared for the project's good execution. MAT will also ensure that confidentiality agreements 
and all the partners’ defined IPRs (foreground and background) in the Co nsortium Agreement (CA) are fully 
respected. MAT will additionally assist with IPR protection activities, in view of strategically protecting the most 
compelling innovation from BioSPRINT, when the IP owners request MAT to do so.

Relevant Projects 
1. For Dutch DSM and Italy based GF Biochemicals MAT conducted a detailed process design and evaluation 
study of new technology for production of Levulinic acid by thermochemical conversion of 
lignocellulose. In order to  support their development, work a comprehensive process design study of the 
Levulinic acid production process is conducted. A number of process options for lignocellulose pre-treatment, 
reaction and product/by-product separation are considered and evaluated. Detailed mass end energy balances, 
technology design and comparison, energy  efficiency studies, economic evaluation, CAPEX, OPEX and 
financial analysis have been conducted to support the project development and business decisions. 
2. For UK based consortium Invista (UK)/ Lanza Tech (UK)/CPI (UK) which is developing new fermentation 
technology for production of butadiene and other value intermediates from waste gases  Maturus Optimi 
conducted process design and economic evaluation study. In order to evaluate technological and economic 
viability of the project, a complete design of the gas fermentation and product separation process has to be 
developed and valuated. To achieve this, the following task have to be completed: development of process 
concept for the complete waste to chemicals plant, detailed mass and energy balance of the plant, technology 
selection and preliminary equipment design, energy study and optimization, full scale economic evaluation of 
the project (CAPEX, OPEX and Financial Analysis). In addition to the main plant, a similar study has been 
performed for the OBL parts of the plant which include connections to the waste gas source, waste gas 
compression and storage.            
3. Dutch startup IONIQA which developed a proprietary technology for chemical recycle of PET (Polyethylene 
terephthalate) is looking to attract investors and therefore needs to demonstrate that the technology is sound 
and economically viable at the commercial scale. For this purpose , Maturus Optimi performed a scale up 
study, design and economic evaluation of commercial scale plant for chemical recycling of PET  
(Polyethylene terephthalate).  Our scope of work included:  Process concept development, design and techno-
economic evaluation of chemical recycle PET plant; Project investment appraisal; Detailed simulation model 
development for technology analysis, drafting process alternatives and process equipment preliminary design; 
Model based planning and support of scale up activities from lab to pilot (100 lit.) to demo (10 k ta) scale; 
Development of Basis of Design (BOD) document for contractors and conceptual design phase.  
4. For a US based developer of gasification technology Anellotech, Maturus Optimi has performed an integral 
process design and economic evaluation study of lignin gasification process into olefins and aromatics. 
Our scope of work included: development of process concept, design of biomass gasifier, catalyst recovery 
unit and downstream processing i.e. separation of light olefins, B,T,N and X; Process modellin g and 
simulation, development and tuning of process mass and energy balance, process analysis for different 
scenarios of lignin conversion and product selectivity ; Process optimization studies, including energy 
efficiency and heat and process integration study (Pinch analysis) of the Gasification and Downstream 
processing units; Creating of BOD document, full scale economic feasibility study: CAPEX, OPEX and 
investment appraisals for several process alternatives.  
5. For companies Roquette and DSM, Maturus Op timi has conducted a full -scale evaluation of yeast-based 
fermentation technology for production of succinic acid from plant derived starch/sugar feedstock  including 
comparison with other fermentation based technologies. Scope of work included: development  of process 
concept, technology selection and design of biobased succinic acid production based low pH yeast 
fermentation, including feedstock pre -treatment, product separation and purification, waste water treatment 
and other auxiliary production facilities. Project scope building and valuation study including AACE level 4 
cost estimate, economic and financial analysis, comparison with bacteria -based fermentation technology for 
production of Succinic acid.

4.1.10 OULUN YLIOPISTO 
Short Name UOULU 
 
Country Finland 
Type Academic 
Website www.UOULU.fi 
Short Profile 
OULUN YLIOPISTO (UOULU) is a multidisciplinary university with 16,000 students and over 3,000 employees 
located in the north of Finland. The university has eight faculties which range from humanities and medicine to 
business, science and technology. The structure of the Univers ity and its wide collaboration network allows it to 
build multidisciplinary projects, conduct high level research and contribute to solving global challenges in the 
following five focus areas:  
1) Creating sustainability through materials and systems;  
2) Molecular and environmental basis for lifelong health;  
3) Digital solutions in sensing and interactions;  
4) Earth and near-space system and environmental change and  
5) Understanding humans in change. 
 
UOULU collaborates in many ways with various partners to meet the changing demands of information and work 
life, and to promote well -being and competitiveness of the society. UOULU has a proven track record of 
participating in the EU Framework programmes throug hout their evolution since FP4. Currently, UOULU 
coordinates 15 European projects. In the Horizon 2020 programme only, the University has more than 75 approved 
projects.  
 
UOULU is well equipped to manage large -scale projects with multiple international pa rtners. To support the 
talented researchers and high -quality infrastructures, the University provides  a range of support services to 
facilitate successful management and implementation of its  multiple projects. Research Support Services, Legal 
Services and Innovation Services help  the researchers in contract, project management, commercialisation and 
IPR-issues. 
 
The participating unit is the Environmental and Chemical Engineering Research Unit (ECE) from the Faculty of 
Technology. The research unit comprises several teams bringing expertise from various fields of engineering, such 
as separation technology, catalyst and  reactor design, sustainability assessment, process modeling, control and 
optimization and  intelligent methods in process automation.  UOULU has versatile expertise in separation 
processes, including membrane technologies (micro -, ultra - and nanofiltration, reverse osmosis and 
pervaporation), distillation, absorption, adsorption and ion-exchange, photocatalysis and ScCO2 extraction based 
on former projects in several application areas.  
 
In addition, UOULU has expertise in photocatalytic membrane separation. The knowhow on heterogeneous 
catalysis is long-lasting both in environmental and process catalysis, which helps to understand the needs set to 
the up-stream purification and separation processes and supports also our modeling group in their studies. UOULU 
has strong experience on utilization of design of experiments and machine learning algorithms, such as automatic 
variable selection methods, artificial neural networks (ANN) and genetic algorithms (GA) with a wide application 
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 109 
 
field. The earliest work stem from 1990s. Further, UOULU holds expertise in process modeling, control and soft 
sensing and recently UOULU has been involved in developing process control tools for intensified processes in 
H2020SPIRE –project. Sustainability assessment, criteria development and process safety are as well mastered by 
the process engineers in the group with the methodological expertise provided by the Industrial Engineering and 
Management Research Unit. 
 
UOULU is an Associate Member of the Bio-based Industries Consortium (BIC) which represents the private sector 
in the Bio-based Industries Joint Undertaking (BBI JU), the Public-Private Partnership (PPP) with the European 
Commission. 
Role in the project 
UOULU will lead WP1 ‘Intensification of Upstream Purification’ aiming to perform the analysis of feedstocks 
establishing technical composition specifications, and analytical comparisons; obtain a stream free of solids 
suitable to be fed to membranes systems; establish a hybrid membrane purification system for the removal of 
inorganic and organic impurities and concentration of hemicelluloses; develop robust systems for handling of 
viscous and solid streams in the process; enhance water and solvent reuse strategies; generate experimental data 
for the validation of the process system engineering tools. In particular, in the analysis of treated hemicellulose 
streams UOULU will specifically leverage its existing expertise in PAT, providing time-on-stream information to 
the operators of bio -refineries. In addition, UOULU will focus on membran e purification as an intrinsically 
intensified separation technology by testing different membrane materials so as to select the best membranes. In 
addition to membranes, UOULU will combine hybrid processes where membrane purification with conventional 
purification processes may be needed in order to explore how the streams may be fractioned by combining micro-
, ultra- and nanofiltration in series. Within WP1, UOULU will also be in charge of the water recovery to improve 
the water efficiency of biorefineries by recovering and reusing the water streams originated from different stages 
of the purification process. 
 
In WP2 ‘Intensification of Catalytic Conversion’, UOULU will lead the task dedicated to catalyst Development 
using HTP Methods aiming to deliver robust catalyst formulations for integrated conversion of C5 and C6 sugars 
into a single reactor, coupled with extraction of reactive furan intermediated. Based on assets from FUNBARK, 
UOULU will develop machine learning algorithms including variable selecti on, evolutionary optimisation, 
intelligent model identification and model validation . The resulted models will be employed to create predictive 
ability between experimental data and accelerate catalyst development and optimisation.  
 
Under WP3 ‘Intensification of Downstream Purification’ , UOULU will be in charge of the i dentification of 
downstream scale-up challenges. Process system engineering (PSE) tools can prevent some typical shortcomings 
of the scale-up of the units from the laboratory to final commercial scale. Data from experimental laboratory results 
will be collected/ analysed to define PSE target. Then, the analysis of distillation (and extraction), using CFD 
tools, as well as the validation with experiments will be performed, also considering the control/PAT development 
for units. UOULU will provide a set of the recommendations for the successful scale -up process of downstream 
purification processes/separation PSE. 
 
In WP4 ‘Development of Biorenewable Resins and Polymerisation Intensi fication’, UOULU will be involved 
in the identification of polymerisation scale-up challenges via process systems engineering tools.  
 
Within WP5 ‘Validation, Process Simulation & Integration’ , UOULU will participate in the s imulation and 
analysis of the e xisting and improved biorefinery processes  supporting the development and testing of the 
simulation models, and assist in linking the results from the plant -wide biorefinery simulations and work 
conducted in WP1-4 and WP6-7. UOULU will also assist DEC to perform a transferability and replicability case 
study using the stream of associated partner Clariant taking the lead on the t ransferability tests for intensified 
technologies. 
 
In WP6 ‘Integrated Lifecycle Sustainability Assessment’ , UOULU will lead the Process and product safety 
assessment, addressing both regulatory and technical barriers. The analysis will utilize quantitative and qualitative 
risk assessment techniques such as fault tree analysis, machinery safety criteria and Hazop (hazard and operability 
study) to identify potential process safety risks and occupational accident and health hazards. As a result, UOULU 
will produce a list of identified safety hazards and an analysis focusing on their risk assessment.

extraction unit and fraction and micro distillation units. In addition, UOULU has a hybrid photocatalytic membrane 
unit.

Short Profile 
PREFERE RESINS GERMANY GMBH  (PFR) is part of the Prefere Resins Group , the leading European 
manufacturer of high quality phenolic, specialty urea and melamine resins. In the Erkner site, mainly resoles and 
novolacs are produced.  
 
Product development is a key focus area for PFR, generating new innovative products and applications as well as 
customised existing products to meet customer’s needs. High emphasis is placed on sustainability, emission 
reduction and alternative products. With a number of product development facilities in Germany, Finland, Austria, 
and the U.S. PFR develop resins, additives, and solutions to enable and support customers with their products and 
innovation processes. experienced specialists make sure that these products are at the forefront of technology and 
constantly adapted to the changing needs of the industries. PFR’s target of development is to provide products 
fulfilling high demands on performance, legal and environmental requirements. Utilization of renewables as raw 
material is a main topic among others in PFR’s development work over last decades. 
 
As one of the global market leaders , PFR supplies its customers with a wide range of tailor -made resins for a 
number of different applications in construction, insulation and in technical applications.

PFR maintains a long tradition of minimising the environmental impact of its processes and products focusing

production processes, as well as producing more environmentally sound products, represent a competitive

environmental management system according to the European Eco-Management and Audit Scheme (EMAS).

As part of WP5 ‘Validation, Process Simulation & Integration’, PFR will be involved in the scale-up of optimal 
product formulations. The most promising polyols, pre -polymers and resins produced by AEP and PFR will be 
selected, characteristics benchmarked, and their developed syntheses replicated through the multiple repeatable 
batches in small –medium bench scale (1 –3 kg) in order to analyse optimal process conditions, assess average 
standard QC properties, and define preliminary tentative specification, thus setting the premises for the scale -up 
to a near-industrial pilot level. 
 
Under WP6 ‘Integrated Lifecycle Sustainability Assessment’, PFR will take part in the process and product safety 
assessment supporting AEP to assess the safety of new bio -based products, taking into account also their 
production processes. 
 
In WP7 ‘Dissemination and Exploitation ’, PFR will support the Coordinator in the Multidimensional 
dissemination, communication and stakeholder engagement activities in order to develop the project’s 
multidimensional dissemination & communication  (D&C) plan and undertake stakeholder base building and 
stakeholder engagement activities via BBI-JU. 
 
PFR will lead: 
− T4.1 Development and testing of novolac-and resole-type resins and their applications in wood laminates

4.1.12 UNIVERSITY OF NEWCASTLE UPON TYNE 
Short Name UNEW  
Country United Kingdom 
Type Academic 
Website www.ncl.ac.uk 
Short Profile 
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 114 
 
UNIVERSITY OF NEWCASTLE UPON TYNE (UNEW) is a Higher Education Institution in the United 
Kingdom. It is part of the Russell Group, which represents 24 leading UK universities which are committed to 
maintaining the very best research and outstanding teaching and learning experience. There are currently 24,696 
undergraduate and post-graduate students registered on full-time and part-time courses at the University. UNEW 
employs a total of 5,786 staff.  
 
UNEW will involve its Process Intensification Group. The Process Intensification Group is part of the School 
Engineering in the Faculty of Science, Agriculture and Engineering (SAgE). The PI group is part of the discipline 
area of Chemical En gineering and currently has 1 5 members of research active academic staff, 9 research 
associates and 42 PhD students, being currently the largest group working on process intensification in the world. 
In particular, the PI Group counts the membership of:  
 
− Prof Adam Harvey, Professor of Process Intensification; 
− Prof David Reay, Senior Research Associate; 
 
The concept of Process intensification (PI) centres on orders of magnitude reductions in the size of process 
equipment, leading to substantial capital and running costs savings, and enabling new processes to break through 
competitive markets. The PI group at Newcastle has been developing novel approaches to equipment design and 
process synthesis with the aim of miniaturising process plants and making these environmentally friendly. The   
group’s research activities involve spinning disc reactors  (SDRs), 
rotating packed beds, oscillatory baffled reactors, micro -reactors, 
plasma reactors, intensified bioreactors, and compact heat 
exchangers among other technologies. UNEW has also developed 
experience in design, synthesis and industrial applications of 
heterogeneous catalysts, and in green chemistry and biorenewable 
processes. The Group has experience in designing intensified 
technologies to address separation processes such as liquid -liquid 
extractions and absorption/desorption in CO 2 sequestration 
applications in high gravity systems which are of direct relevance. 
UNEW is also developing technology for sustainable processing 
applications, including research on CO 2 capture and valorisation 
using heterogeneous catalysts and photo/bio/electrical catalysts. The 
Group have experience in planning and conducting prototype, pilot 
and full scale plant test work for validation of lab scale technologies 
and scale up of equipment. 
 
With regards to Brexit, UNEW remains committed to participation in H2020 and hope that the UK reaches an 
agreement allowing continued participation in H2020 and successor programmes. In case this proves impossible, 
the UK government has made public assurances that “where UK organisations bid directly to the EC (…) for EU 
funding projects while [the UK is] still a member of the EU, the Treasury will underwrite the payments, even when 
specific projects continue beyond the UK’s departure from the EU . In addition, it announced the gu arantee is 
extended to the end of 2020, even in a no deal scenario.  
Role in the project 
UNEW will also play a major role in development of continuous and intensified methods of upstream purification, 
catalytic conversion, downstream purification and polymerization. UNEW will contribute with inputs to process 
simulation, LCA, economical assessment, dissemination and exploitation activities. Most importantly, UNEW will 
undertake Technical Management for the project, ensuring technical work is appropriately coordinated across all 
WPs and directly contributes to the realisation of the project’s impact. 
 
In WP1 ‘Intensification of Upstream Purification’ , UNEW will design the precipitation and solids handling 
processes. In particular, UNEW will be in charge of the intensification of precipitation using Spinning Disc 
Reactors and the o ptimisation of partic le formation for enhanced solids recovery . UNEW will also support 
UOULU in the hybrid membrane purification and concentration of hemicelluloses sugars activities. 
 
UNEW will lead WP2 ‘Intensification of Catalytic Conversion’, aiming to: develop robust predictive models for 
catalyst composition and catalysts for simultaneous C5 and C6 sugars dehydration; develop kinetic models to 
describe the conversion and aqueous-organic partition of multiple C5/C6 sugars; intensify the dehydration reaction

by integration of the conversion of multiple C5 and C6 sugars to furans in a single unit ; investigate the effect of

As part of WP3 ‘Intensification of Downstream Puri fication’, UNEW will participate in the p reparatory 
processing actions for downstream and lead the intensification of downstream purification processes focusing in 
the reduction in foot print and hazardous inventory for the liquid -liquid decanter unit that separates the aqueous 
and the organic phases with an emphasis on the intensification and integration of heat transfer in distillation units.  
 
In WP4 ‘Development of Biorenewable Resins and Polymerisation Intensification’, UNEW will support AEP in 
the development of rigid foams from bio-based polyols under which new resins and polyols developed as part of 
WP4 will be used in industrial reference formulations for thermosetting adhesives and fibre-reinforced composites 
and for rigid polyurethane foams. In addition, UNEW will lead the process intensification of bio-based polymer 
production. Based on the formulations developed for the bio-based novolac-type resins and Mannich-type polyols, 
which will be studied in conventional batch stirred tank reactor technologies, protocols will be developed to 
transfer the optimised formulations to a continuously operated polymerisation process with a view to upscaling 
the production of selected polymers from grams to kg scale. 
 
In WP5 ‘Validation, Process Simulation & Integration’ UNEW will be involved in the simulation and analysis 
of the existing and improved biorefinery processes  supporting the development and testing  of the simulations 
models, and assist in linking the results from the plant-wide biorefinery simulations and work conducted in WP1-
4 and WP6-7. UNEW will also assist UPM and FhG to integrate the developed concepts and technologies for the 
UPM stream and the FhG Organosolv streams respectively.  
 
As part of WP7 ‘Dissemination and Exploitation’, UNEW will be actively involved in the development of the 
project’s multidimensional dissemination & communication (D&C) plan an d the delivery of the D&C activities. 
In addition, UNEW will support NIC in order to develop and deliver a scalable training and capacity -building 
programme, in particular UNEW will organise one capacity -building workshop at its premises in Year 2 of the 
project. UNEW will also contribute to existing and emerging standards by supporting DEC with the establishment 
of a CENELEC Workshop Agreement on ‘PI for biorefining processes’.  
 
In WP8 ‘Project coordination’, will support the project Coordinator in the overall coordination, reporting and 
management, as leader of WP2. Moreover, UNEW will undertake the role of Technical Management, leveraging 
Process Intensification expertise . UNEW will  monitor the technical progress of the project according to the 
contractual schedule; the preparation of technical deliverables . UNEW will p rovide technical expertise in the 
coordination and steering of efforts in the technical WPs, while assisting in the technical soundness and feasibility 
assessment of all the project’s tasks.

Key Personnel 
Dr. Fernando J Russo Abegão (male) is a Teaching Fellow in the School of Chemical Engineering and Advanced 
Materials. Fernando holds a Licenciatura degree in Chemical Engineering, University of Coimbra, Portugal and a 
PhD degree from the University of Cambridge, UK. Fernando’s research focus is on catalysis and reaction 
engineering with a particular interest in process intensification and  biorenewable applications. Current work 
applications include process intensification of biodiesel and glycerol conversion processes, CO2 conversion into 
chemicals and fuels, photocatalysis, catalytic upgrade of biomass, and intensified synthesis of hetero geneous 
catalysts. Fernando is a CoI in a Marie Skłodowska -Curie Innovative Training Networks – CHARMING – 
Chemical Engineering Immersive Learning, 500k EUR (H2020-MSCA-ITN-2018, proposal number 812716). He 
has also been awarded 5 research early career res earch grants over the last 3 academic years on a total of £90k. 
Fernando has an extensive background in industrial catalysis. He worked for Johnson Matthey as a Senior Research 
Scientist and as a Process Development Engineer investigating catalyst manufact uring processes and developing 
a new generation of manufacturing methods. He has coordinated multiple industrial trials involving partners across 
Europe and he led the technical design of a multi -million pounds state -of-the-art facility for manufacture of 
heterogeneous catalyst. Additionally, he managed the upgrade and commissioning of two manufacturing lines. 
Fernando also worked on development and design of Platinum Group Metal catalysts for several chemical, 
petrochemical and biorenewable applications, h aving taken part in the development of the formulation of 4 
commercial heterogeneous catalysts.  Dr. Fernando will be the Leader of WP2 ‘Intensification of Catalytic 
Conversion’. 
 
Dr. Kamelia Boodhoo (female) is a Reader in Sustainable Process Technology within the Chemical Engineering 
stream in the School Engineering at Newcastle University, UK. Her expertise is on the development of continuous 
flow reactors with particular emphasis on centrifugal field reactors such the Spinning Disc Reactor (SDR) and 
their application to a range of processes involving polymerisation, crystallisation, polymerisation and organic 
catalytic reactions. Since 2001, she has secured over £1M of research income as PI and Co -I. The most recent 
award in 2015 was €640k of funding as PI for the “Intensified by Design (IbD)” project supported by Horizon2020 
SPIRE-8 Programme as part of a large consortium of 22 EU academic and industrial partners (Total project funding 
€8.5M). In the last 15 years, she has attracted over £200k of industri al funding from multinational organisations 
such as Total Oil, Roquette Freres and Eastman Chemicals. Between 2004 and 2018, she has successfully 
supervised 10 full-time PhD students and 6 postdoctoral researchers in the area of process intensification, spinning 
disc reactor, polymerisation, crystallisation and fermentation processes. She is currently supervising a further 3 
PhD students. She has published over 35 peer-reviewed articles in leading scientific journals, 7 book chapters and 
more than 30 confer ence papers. She is the lead editor of “Process Intensification for Green Chemistry: 
Engineering Solutions for Sustainable Processing” (Wiley -Blackwell, 2013).  Dr. Kamelia will serve as the 
Technical Manager. 
 
Maureen Wilkinson (Female) is a Chief Informat ion Security Officer at UNEW. She is an experienced 
Data/Information Governance Manager with a demonstrated history of working in the Health Sector, Higher 
Education and utilities industry. She is skilled in Data Protection, Incident Management, Informatio n Risk 
Management, Strategy, Information Security Governance and IT Service Processes. Maureen will serve as the 
Data Protection Officer of UNEW.

4.1.13 UPM GMBH 
Short Name UPM

Type Industrial
