Short Profile 
UPM GMBH (UPM) is a global leader of the bio-based forest industry with a history dating back over 100 years. 
Through the renewing of the bio and forest industries, UPM is building a sustainable future across six business 
areas: UPM Biorefining, UPM Energy, UPM Raflatac , UPM Specialty Papers, UPM Paper ENA and UPM 
Plywood. UPM’s products are made of renewable raw materials and are recyclable. Today, UPM is serving 
thousands of customers worldwide employing around 19,300 people with annual sales exceeding EUR 10 billion. 
UPM shares are listed on NASDAQ OMX Helsinki. 
 
Figure 4: Rotating Packed Bed 
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 118 
 
UPM’s extensive knowledge and know-how of sustainably sourced renewable wood biomass is the starting point 
of their business. UPM sees versatile wood-based biochemicals as the next natural step in the evolutio n of wood 
usage. Wood-based renewable biochemicals offer sustainable and competitive high-quality solutions for replacing 
fossil-based raw materials. UPM’s responsibly sourced renewable lignin is already in use across various industries 
and applications.  
 
UPM provides Glycols and Lignin products. UPM has developed an advanced concept for the production of 
renewable glycols targeting sustainable performance. Furthermore, Lignin is a versatile biomaterial that helps to 
reduce dependency on fossil -based raw materials as we’re moving from disposable to sustainable. That’s why 
lignin has already found its way into a rapidly growing number of industrial applications such as resins, adhesives, 
bio-plastics, and polyurethanes.  
 
Following five years of extensive technology development and piloting, UPM is currently evaluating the potential 
of a new-to-the-world biorefinery that would convert hardwood from sustainably managed forests into renewable 
glycols and lignin.  The planned industrial scale biorefinery would convert wood into bio -monoethylene glycol 
(bMEG), bio-monopropylene glycol (bMPG) and lignin up to 150,000 metric tons per year. Production would be 
based on hardwood from sustainably managed forests in Central Europe.  
 
Role in the project 
UPM is interested to support the development within the project by providing knowhow in the field of 
lignocellulosic based sugar production and techno -economic evaluation of biorefinery processes. Furthermore, 
UPM will provide samples obtained from UPMs operations as industrial relevant feedstock available. 
Theerfore, UPM’role is four-fold: 
1) Provision of hemicellulose streams for purification and further processing 
2) Provision of expertise and specifications for the WP on upstream purification 
3) Leading the validation activities 
4) Contribution to the Techno-economic analysis of the project’s results (process performance, market viability, 
value chain compatibility) 
5) Contribution to dissemination and exploitation of projects’ results. 
 
As an industrial feedstock provider, in WP1 ‘Intensification of Upstream Purification’, UPM will contribute in 
the analysis of treated hemicellulose streams by supplying a hardwood hemicellulose stream from biorefinery pilot 
operations. UPM will take part in the precipitation and solids handling processes. Moreover, UPM will be involved 
in the h ybrid membrane purification and concentration of hemicelluloses sugars . UPM will provide its  
hemicellulose stream which stems from solid-liquid separation after the pre-treatment step without any additional 
purification so it contains larger amounts of soluble lignin, furans, organic acids, soluble ash, and pre -treatment 
chemicals. 
 
UPM will lead WP5 ‘Validation, Process Simulation & Integration’ , which aims to analyse and simulate the 
existing and BioSPRINT biorefinery process; integrate the developed concepts and technologies for the UPM 
stream and the FhG Organosolv streams; perform a transferability and replicability case study using the stream of 
associated partner Clariant; and also proceed with optimisation and first upscaling of the best synthetic products. 
In particular, UPM will participate in the simulation and analysis of the existing and improved biorefinery 
processes and be in charge of the i ntegration of the developed concepts and technologies for its stream with an 
emphasis into the validation of the upstream purification technologies for removal of lignin and potential catalyst 
inhibitors. Upon completion, a technology-transfer report will be produced indicating the prospect of integrating 
the realised intensified process into UPM biorefining operations.  
 
In WP6 ‘Integrated Lifecycle Sustainability Assessment’ , UPM will be involved in the t echno-economic 
assessment supporting MAT in developing economic models of the improved biorefinery, with PI technologies 
implemented.  
 
Under WP7 ‘Dissemination and Exploitation’ , UPM will, with rest of the partners, actively participate in the 
dissemination and communication activities in order to develop the project’s multidimensional dissemination & 
communication (D&C) plan also supporting MAT to identify early adopters and post-project opportunities. UPM 
will also contribute to existing and emerging standards by taking part in the meetings of technical committees for 
standardisation whose scope is relevant to BioSPRINT.

use of renewable feedstocks in the process industry, processing of dilute complex aqueous mixtures. Under 
the consortial leadership of BASF, nine partners including U PM, from UK, Germany, Finland, Belgium and 
the Netherlands collaborated. (01/01/2015 – 31/12/2018) www.spire2030.eu/prodias.

Section 5: Ethics and Security
5.1 Ethics 
 
The research carried out in the project, even though primarily focused on chemical and biochemical processes, will 
involve human participants who will be  volunteers and who will give informed consent to participation in the 
research. All participants will be provided with a sheet informing them about the handling of their data before the 
start of the study  (Annex 3), which will then be signed and returned, constituting informed co nsent. There are no 
exclusion or inclusion criteria besides recruitment criteria related to a useful adequate sample covering the topics of 
the study.  
 
During the preparation of this proposal, in keeping with the required Ethics Appraisal Procedure, an Et hics Self-
assessment was performed with the completion of the Ethical Issues Table, and this project does not involve specific 
Ethics issues.  
Although the self -assessment identified no ethics issues arising from the actual workplan itself, it is worthy of  
comment the measures that we are taking during the project work plan to address and mitigate any concerns that 
could indeed appear in the future:  
• Regulatory activities have been incorporated in the project with the intention of gathering data to fuel into a 
further safe and compliant development phase. See T6.5 ‘Process and product safety assessment’, addressing 
both regulatory and technical barriers on page 59 in section 3.   
• The appropriate health and safety procedures conforming to relevant local/national guidelines/legislation will 
be followed by staff involved in this project. In this sense, partners follow recognised hygiene and safety 
rules, including sectorial rules. For example, end-users in the Chemicals sector abide to chemical regulations 
such as REACH.  See page 23 in section 1.   
• The use of LCSA, which identifies environmental as well as social, health and safety impacts, can help 
identify where the maximum impact could occur providing the opportunity for process or material 
modifications to minimise these impacts. See page 37 in section 2.   
• Finally measures related to responsible innovation, spread as relevant along the work plan, are overseen in 
WP8 (T8.4 Innovation, IPR & Data Management).  
 
BioSPRINT aims at utilising and valorising hemicelluloses, pursuing intensified processing steps and technologies 
towards ‘zero -waste’ bio -based operations and applying an integrated biorefinery concept that embodies the 
cascading principle to create new hemicellulose-derived products, so as to maximise conversion of the lignocellulosic 
biomass feedstock and its by -products, side streams and residual streams into higher added -value products. The 
BioSPRINT philosophy is based on valorising the previously -discarded or costly side streams (thus ‘closing the 
loop’).  The purpose of the BioSPRINT project is to develop, test and validate process intensification methods (up to 
TRL 4-5) for purification and conversion of sugars from the hemicellulose fraction of lignocellulosic biomass to 
obtain biorenewable furan-based resins for novel polymeric applications. 
To do so, BioSPRINT works directly with researchers and professionals in Process Intensification technologies and 
Biotechnology as well professi onals from the Bioeconomy, standardisation and regulatory bodies, ICT SMEs, 
feedstock providers, etc.  
 
The project will thus work directly with employees of organisations listed above, and will conform to established 
ethical principles when doing research and development with human subjects as well as development of innovative 
systems and methods. The BioSPRINT Platform will also use behavioural and educational data from and about 
participants.  
 
Should the BioSPRINT activities raise social and ethical issues due to the sensitive nature of this data as well as the 
nature of the technologies involved, for example related to the following: 
• Personal data handling, which will be done in accordance to the General Data Protection Regulation 
(Regulation 2016/679) (GDPR);  
• Developing systems and advancing the state of the art responsibly (i.e. not pursue research and innovation 
that could in any way be detrimental to persons, society or environment).  
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 123 
 
The Project Coordinator and the consortium will take all appropri ate measures to address them efficiently. As a 
testimony of this commitment, a subtask of the project ST8. 4.3 ‘Ethics, Gender and cross -cutting priority 
monitoring’ (WP8) is dedicated to monitor ethics and cross-cutting-priorities .  
 
At proposal stage, th e consortium members have agreed that the work that will be performed are driven by the 
following key ethical frameworks:  
• The Universal Declaration of Human Rights and the Convention 108 for the Protection of Individuals with 
Regard to Automatic Processing of Personal Data; 
• the Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union (2000/C 364/01); 
• the European Convention on Human Rights; 
• The European Code of Conduct for Research Integrity; 
• Horizon 2020 Rules for Participation; 
• Principles and guidelines of “Ethics for Researchers” to Facilitate Research Excellence, prepared by the EC 
Governance and Ethics Unit in 2007. 
• The association of Internet Researchers guidelines and as well as guidelines from ethical review boards (those 
present at academic institutions of the project).  
 
As part of the project, we will aim to identify, analyse and integrate considerations of any legal, ethical or social 
issues raised by the project, and identify and implement elements that will foster trust, usability and social acceptance. 
 
The consideration of ethical issues, and the embedding of ethics -by-design, is a key way in which BioSPRINT 
represents progress beyond the state of the art. Our ethics-by-design approach applies to the assessment of research 
and innovation plans and practices. It aims at encouraging all partners involved in the course of research and 
innovation as part of the project to: 
  
• Anticipate and consider the potential consequences of the research and innovation project for society, 
including any plausible future uses and applications of the results of project, and take appropriate remedial 
action to address any (potentially) negative societal and environmental impacts if such action seems justified; 
• Consider whether and how the research or innovation activity could positively or negatively contribute to the 
interests, rights and well-being of individuals and groups 
• Consider whether the research or innovation promotes or is compatible with sustainable development, and 
how it might promote greater environmental sustainability; 
• Avoid misuse of research materials and results. Consider whether the materials, methods, technologies, and 
knowledge involved in or generated during the research or innovation could serve, or be modified or 
enhanced to serve, individuals, animals, society and/or the environment 
• Communicate important research results and (potential) societal consequences to relevant stakeholders and 
to the general public to ensure their proper interpretation, while explaining the degree of uncertainty 
involved. 
 
Given this, the consortium of BioSPRINT is committed to handling potential ethical issues responsibly. All partners 
will adhere to and respect national regulations and laws and will continue to reflect and refine our own innovation 
conduct, data processing, ethical principles and practices.  
 
Regarding the collection of personal data. The question: “ 4 - Collection of Personal Data - Does your research 
involve personal data collection and/or processing? ” has been answered with ‘Yes’, since several considerations 
related to on-site activities and capacity-building activities shall be taken into consideration.  
 
The BioSPRINT partners are familiar with the ethical requirements associated with research with humans, given their 
training and previous experience in research and innovation methodology, and are familiar with the sorts of processes 
needed to meet and exceed these requirements. 
 
For example, in relation to informed consent, the consortium will adhere to the following principles: 
• All the test subjects, and their legal guardians where applicable, will be informed and given the opportunity to 
provide their consent to any monitoring and data acquisition process that all the subjects will be strictly volunteers 
and all test volunteers receive detailed oral information. 
• All stakeholder engagement activities ( testing, trials, workshops, etc.) will be conducte d with participants that 
will be in a position to understand their role in the project, what data is collected, how it is processed, stored and 
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 124 
 
anonymised and peer reviewed before being used in the project used e.g. through publication or as part of system 
innovation. No covert data collection will take place. 
• No data will be collected without the explicit informed consent of the individuals under observation and their 
legal guardian where applicable. This involves being open with participants about what th ey are involving 
themselves in and ensuring that they have agreed fully to the procedures/research being undertaken by giving 
their explicit consent. 
• Participants will be given information on who will benefit from their participation in the research and what risk 
or burden they are undertaking by participating.  
• The consortium will also provide information about the potential for commercial exploitation of the innovation. 
Participation in these aspects of the BioSPRINT project will be fully voluntary and all participants will be given 
the opportunity to ask questions and receive understandable answers before making decisions about their 
participation.  
• Participants will also have the right to withdraw and terminate their participation in the research at any 
time and will be reminded about their rights before participation. Participants will be given this information via 
an information sheet and be asked to sign a consent form to document and verify the information they have been 
given. During the research, in formed consent forms will be used for pilot testing and workshops with experts. 
The BioSPRINT Draft Information sheet and informed consent form are provided in the Optional Annex 3: 
Ethics supporting document(s). These sheets will be continually reviewed b y the consortium, and respective 
ethics committees that will need to approve any pilots, trials, workshops etc. 
• No personal or sensitive data will be centrally stored. In addition, data will be scrambled where possible and 
abstracted in a way that will not affect the final project outcome. 
• No data collected will be sold or used for any purposes other than the current project. 
• A data minimisation policy will be adopted at all levels of the project and will be supervised by the Project 
Coordinator and the Data Protection Officers appointed by each partner. This will ensure that no data which is 
not strictly necessary to the completion of the current study will be collected. 
• Specific measures will be in place in order to protect the pupils from a breach of privacy/confidentiality and any 
potential discrimination; In particular their names will not be made public and their participation will not be 
communicated to. Any incidental findings will be kept strictly confidential and erased from files under request 
from the enrolled subject.  
 
5.1.1 Meeting national requirements  
With specific relation to national ethical requirements, BioSPRINT will undertake specific reviews of the innovation 
to be brought forward. First, BioSPRINT will be guided by the ethical codes of partners such as those of DEC, 
UOULU, UNEW, NIC, etc. In addition, BioSPRINT will fully comply to specific (and in certain cases more strict) 
national legislation of the countries involved in the project.  
 
Our starting point is a peer-reviewed approach to ethics, in which policies, protocols, innovation and data handling 
is reviewed by peers with different skillsets, perspectives, which is informed by all other ethical frameworks to make 
informed decisions about any ethical concerns. As part of this process, if necessary, we will conduct a Data Protection 
Impact Assessment (DPIA) on the project to help identify and minimise the data protection risks of a project.  
 
Should the EC request national assessments in addition to these mechanisms, the Project Coordinator will liaise with 
the Project Officer to identify potential review mechanisms. All reviews will include a consideration of the objectives, 
methodology and potential impact of the activities undertaken in the BIOSPRINT project. This robust review cycle 
will ensure that the project complies with national and European legislati on (including privacy and data protection 
legislation) and with the ethical principles associated with research with humans and Responsible Research and 
Innovation principles. Subtasks ST8.1.3 External Advisory Board management and ST8.3.4 ‘Ethics, Gender and 
cross-cutting priority monitoring’, will ensure that project’s research activities are ethically sound and that data from 
research participants is stored according to EU and national regulations to ensure their privacy.  
 
Where required, this task will also seek approval from relevant national authorities. Throughout the project, the 
implementation of the Ethics protocol will be monitored and reported on in the project’s interim and final reviews 
(M18 and M36). All ethical issues pertaining to these reviews will be forwarded to the Project Steering Team for 
discussion and action.  
 
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
                                                                                                                                                                      Page 125 
 
5.1.2 Data collection  
The BioSPRINT project will touch on privacy and data protection issues by collecting data from project participants 
from EU countries via the project workshops and events, collecting data about persons as part of the te st data used 
by the project and collecting data about during the Training, Education & Capacity-Building Programme (TECBP). 
Both qualitative and quantitative data can be collected through these activities. During their implementation we are 
likely to obtain questionnaire and interview data.  
 
Questionnaires and interviews will take place in data collection sessions, in which each participant is always aware 
of that they are being recorded. All digitally recorded activities will be done with participant’s ex plicit consent. In 
addition, we will identify what data will be necessary for the project, and only record and study that relevant for the 
project. 
 
Personal data will be processed anonymously and in an aggregated form where possible. Personal data collected from 
the BioSPRINT project will be treated as highly confidential, respecting privacy  in GDPR compliant manners. In 
these cases, the personnel involved will receive an informed consent, expressed in a formal agreement. BioSPRINT 
will collect and process data that are strictly necessary for the research. All of the individuals participating in the 
project’s activities will be volunteers and will have the project data collection, storage and processing plans explained 
to them before the activity begins. Should they wish to exclude themselves from the activity, or should they wish 
their data to be anonymised after the activity, the consortium will oblige and write to them to confirm (a) that their 
wishes have been carried out and (b) precisely how their wishes have been carried out. 
 
BioSPRINT does not involve the processing of genetic information. 
 
Data storage will be secured and access by unwanted third parties will be prevented. Appropriate procedures will be 
applied for data coll ection (and their usage) and the methodology that will be employed for collecting, using and 
storing various data and information. These procedures include encryption and anonymisation/pseudonymisation/ 
aggregation of sensitive data according to GDPR. Concerning risk management and legal compliance, all participants 
are aware of their obligations as potential data processers and controllers as well as issues beyond data and 
information protection and privacy described above. Actions should be taken to ensur e that those handling subjects 
identifiable or sensitive information are made fully aware of their responsibilities and obligations to respect 
confidentiality in compliance with market standards (e.g.: ISO/IEC 27001:2005), best practices and legal 
requirements under the GDPR. 
 
Data protection legislation, standards and best practices will be applied on the data collection, storage, protection, 
retention and destruction. The related GDPR-compliant procedures for data collection, storage, protection, retention, 
destruction or re -use as well as data safety procedures will be developed as part of Subtask ST8.4.2 ‘Data 
Management plan and monitoring’. In addition,  Subtask ST 8.4.3 ‘Ethics, Gender & cross -cutting priority 
monitoring’ will ensure that BIOSPRINT activities and pilots testing are ethically sound and that data from research 
participants is stored according to EU and national regulations to ensure their privacy. In addition, every partner has 
appointed, or will appoint from project’s start, a Data Protection Officer (DPO). 
 
This does not imply that every partner will indeed engage in data processing activities, but rather ensure that data 
protection obligations resulting from GDPR, if any, will be duly identified and complied with by each partner. 
 
The Parties agree that any Background, Results, Confidential Information and/or any data and/or information that is 
provided, disclosed or otherwise made available between the Parties during the implementation of the Action and/or 
for any Exploitation activities (“Shared Information”), shall not include personal data as defined by Article 4, General 
Data Protection Regulation (679/2016) (hereinafter referred to as “Personal Data”). Accordingly, each Party agrees 
that it will take all necessary steps to ensu re that all Personal Data is removed from the Shared Information, made 
illegible, or otherwise made inaccessible (i.e. de -identify) to the other Parties prior to providing the Shared 
Information to such other Parties.  
 
Most of the documentation associated  with these ethical and legal reviews are not yet available, nor would it be 
appropriate to approach the relevant experts before the project is funded. However, the consortium is happy to provide 
the draft information sheets consent forms to be used by the  project in the Optional Annex 3 – Ethics supporting 
documents. 
 
This proposal version was submitted by Jochen Michels on 04/09/2019 16:25:03 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.

5.2 Security  
 BIOSPRINT will not involve:  
• Activities or results raising security issues;  
• 'EU-classified information' as background or results.  
 
This initial assessment does not preclude a different assessment following the security scrutiny. Should the members 
of the JTI Programme Committee consider that BioSPRINT involves security-related activities or produces outputs 
that need to be classified, special provisions for classified information (as defined in the Commission Ru les of 
Procedure (Decision 2015/444/EC,ECSC,Euratom, and further explained in the Guidelines for the classification of 
research results) will be taken in the grant agreement, as necessary and appropriate.

5.3.2 AEP POLYMERS SRL 
As part of BioSPRINT, work conducted by AEP, exclusively destined to civil applications, will not involve: 
− personal data collection and processing; 
 
AEP uses chemical substances on the laboratory scale for the synthesis of new building blocks and their use in 
formulated systems. All of them have an associated chemical hazard. All researchers at AEP use personal protective 
equipment (PPE) and collective protective equipment (CPE), chosen or designed according to the Safety Data Sheets 
of the substances in use, so neutralizing the risk for health. All researchers are properly trained and subject to 
periodical health surveillance. The level of chemical risk is periodically updated. 
Some chemicals used as reactants are hazardous for the environment. Researchers at AEP  neutralize the  
environmental hazard through proper equipment (e.g. several filters are installed on each laboratory fumehood and 
are periodically replaced to ensure optimal efficiency ) and correct disposal of every liquid or solid waste produced 
in the laboratory by certified companies.

BioSPRINT is a 48-month EU-funded project with the purpose of __________________.  
You are invited to join the BioSPRINT research project to take part in the BioSPRINT definitions/ case studies   
integrated life cycle assessment / dissemination & communication activitie/1. Please take whatever time you need to 
read and understand the following text. The decision to join, or not to join, is up to you. If you agree with the content, 
please sign the consent form hereafter.  
 
I freely and voluntarily consent to participate in the BioSPRINT project.  
The aim of this activity is to _________________________. It will be conducted at _____________. 
I understand that my participation is voluntary and free-of-charge.  
I understand that the project may stop the activity or take me out of the trial at any time they judge it is in my best 
interest. They may also remove me from the trial for various other reasons. They can do this without my consent.  
I am free to stop participating at any time without any negative consequence.  
I understand that the activity will take me approximately _________ minutes/hours.  
I understand that BioSPRINT will process my personal information for the purposes of the project. Only information 
that is necessary to address the central purpose of the research will be recorded, and the data will be anonymised at 
the point of collection. My name or any information that could identify me or relate to my identity will not be linked 
with the research materials. The information will be securely stored and retained for the lifetime of the project and 
safely deleted afterwards.  
I understand that such information will be treated as strictly confidential and handled in accordance with the 
provisions of the Charter of Fundamental Rights of the EU (2000/c 364/01), Convention No. 108 of the Council of 
Europe for the Protection of Individuals and Regulation (EU) 2016/679.  
I have been informed that , if I have any questions about the trial or the project itself, any problems, unexpected 
physical or psychological discomforts, any injuries, or think that something unusual or unexpected is happening I am 
free to contact Mr./Ms. [First Name, Last Name] at mail@example.com.
